1 Introductory Material 1 
1.1 Foreword 2 
This Technical Specification has been produced by the O-RAN Alliance. 3 
The contents of the present document are subject to continuing work within O-RAN and may change following formal 4 
O-RAN approval. Should the O-RAN Alliance modify the contents of the present document, it will be re-released by O-5 
RAN with an identifying change of release date and an increase in version number as follows:  6 
Release x.y.z 7 
where: 8 
x the first digit is incremented for all changes of substance, i.e. technical enhancements, corrections, updates, 9 
etc. (the initial approved document will have x=01). 10 
y the second digit is incremented when editorial only changes have been incorporated in the document.  11 
z the third digit included only in working versions of the document indicating incremental changes during the 12 
editing process. 13 
1.2 Scope 14 
1.2.1 General 15 
The present document defines tests that validate the conformance to the protocols defined in [2] for the Lower Layer 16 
Split Option 7.2x interface between the O-RU and the O-DU.  A guiding principal for these conformance tests is to use 17 
only standard interfaces that are defined by the specification [2] or relevant 3GPP specifications.  The construction of 18 
these tests avoids the requirement for a device to include any special interfaces used solely for the purpose of these 19 
tests. 20 
While these tests are not written to evaluate the performance of an O-DU or O-RU device, some tests require obtaining 21 
measurements and evaluating the success or failure of the device to process sample  data correctly based on portion of 22 
the protocol being tested at the time.     23 
In general, unless otherwise stated, the tests cover LTE (Stand-Alone), NR Non-Stand-Alone (NSA) and NR Stand-24 
Alone (SA).  25 
1.2.2 U-Plane and C-Plane Scope 26 
This version of the Conformance Test specification defines tests which validate the conformance of an O-RU.  The tests 27 
are designed to cover a large number of optional functionalities defined in [2].  Therefore, for any given O-RU 28 
implementation, a subset of these tests may not be applicable.  It is the responsibility of the tester to understand the 29 
applicability of each test to the feature provided by a particular O-RU.    30 
Future versions of this specification may add tests which validate the conformance of a  O-DU and may expand on other 31 
areas not currently addressed in this version. 32 
1.2.3 S-Plane  33 
This version of the Conformance Test specification defines tests for time synchronization of the O-RU.  The tests 34 
defined in this version include both functional tests and performance tests.  Functional tests confirm the ability of the O-35 
RU to achieve the proper synchronization management state based on a variety of PTP  and optionally SyncE input 36 
conditions.  Performance tests validate  the conformance of the recovered clock for the O-RU.   37 
Concerning the scope of the S-Plane, various synchronization options have been defined in the ORAN Specification for 38 
distributing synchronization to the O-RU (LLS-C1, LLS-C2, LLS-C3 and LLS-C4). Depending on the specific ORAN 39 
deployment being considered not all of them may be relevant. When testing the S-Plane, the tester shall identify which 40 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
7 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
of the test cases are relevant depending on the specific deployment scenarios addressed. As a general guideline the 1 
following applies: 2 
1) Direct connection between O-DU and O-RU:  3 
• LLS-C1 is generally the main sync option to be validated.  4 
• LLS-C4 may be considered as alternative or as a complement to C1 5 
 6 
2) Bridged network between O-DU and O-RU 7 
• LLS-C2 for cases where the synchronization is delivered to the O-RU via the O-DU and over the 8 
bridged network. In this case the PRTC/PRC may be embedded in the O-DU or may be located 9 
anywhere in the network (backhaul or fronthaul) 10 
• LLS-C3 for cases when the synchronization is distributed to the O-RU without involving the O-DU In 11 
this case the PRTC/PRC may be located anywhere in the network (backhaul or fronthaul) and may 12 
also be co-located with the O_DU. 13 
• LLS-C4 may be considered as alternative or as a complement to LLS-C2/C3 14 
 15 
 16 
1.2.4 Test Requirement Status 17 
The following table is a list of each test in this conformance specification and status of the test as REQUIRED or 18 
CONDITIONAL MANDATORY.  Note that tests that are REQUIRED are for those functions of the DUT that by 19 
specification are required to be supported.  Optional functionality in a DUT implies that the corresponding conformance 20 
test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY and is mandatory only if the DUT supports the optional functionality.  21

1.3.1 Definitions 2 
For the purposes of the present document, the terms and definitions given in 3GPP TR 21.905, “Vocabulary for 3GPP 3 
Specifications”[1]and the following apply. A term defined in the present document takes precedence over the definitio n 4 
of the same term, if any, in [1] 5 
C-Plane Control Plane: refers specifically to real-time control between O-DU and O-RU, and should not be 6 
confused with the UE’s control plane 7 
DL DownLink: data flow towards the radiating antenna 8 
eNB eNodeB (applies to LTE) <E-UTRAN NodeB / Evolved NodeB> 9 
fm-pm Fault Management, Performance Management role 10 
gNB gNodeB (applies to NR) <Next Generation NodeB> 11 
M-Plane Management Plane: refers to non-real-time management operations between the O-DU and the O-12 
RU 13 
NETCONF Network Configuration Protocol. For details see: RFC 6241, “Network Configuration Protocol 14 
(NETCONF)”, IETF, June 2011 15 
NSA Non-Stand-Alone network mode that supports operation of SgNB attached to MeNB 16 
O-CU O-RAN Central Unit – a logical node hosting PDCP, RRC, SDAP and other control functions 17 
O-DU O-RAN Distributed Unit: a logical node hosting RLC/MAC/High-PHY layers based on a lower 18 
layer functional split. O-DU in addition hosts an M-Plane instance. 19 
O-RU O-RAN Radio Unit <O-RAN Radio Unit: a logical node hosting Low-PHY layer and RF 20 
processing based on a lower layer functional split. This is similar to 3GPP’s “TRP” or “RRH” but 21 
more specific in including the Low-PHY layer (FFT/iFFT, PRACH extraction).>. O-RU in 22 
addition hosts M-Plane instance. 23 
PTP Precision Time Protocol (PTP) is a protocol for distributing precise time and frequency over 24 
packet networks. PTP is defined in the IEEE Standard 1588. 25 
PDCCH Physical Downlink Control Channel applies for LTE and NR air interface  26 
PBCH Physical Broadcast Channel applies for LTE and NR air interface 27 
SA Stand-Alone network mode that supports operation of gNB attached to a 5G Core Network  28 
SCS OFDM Sub Carrier Spacing 29 
SSB Synchronization Signal Block, in 5G PBCH and synchronization signal are packaged as a single 30 
block 31 
sudo Super-User Do role 32 
S-Plane Synchronization Plane: Data flow for synchronization and timing information between nodes 33 
SyncE Synchronous Ethernet, is an ITU-T standard for computer networking that facilitates distribution 34 
of clock signals over the Ethernet physical layer 35 
T-BC Telecom Boundary Clock 36 
TWAMP Two-Way Active Measurement Protocol 37 
UDP User Datagram Protocol 38 
UE User Equipment terminology for a mobile device in LTE and NR 39 
UL UpLink: data flow from the UE towards the core network, that is from the O-RU towards in the O-40 
DU in a Fronthaul context. 41

1.3.2 Abbreviations 1 
For the purposes of the present document, the following abbreviations apply.  2 
 3 
C-Plane Control Plane: refers specifically to real-time control between O-DU and O-RU, and should not be 4 
confused with the UE’s control plane 5 
CUSM-E C-Plane, U-Plane, S-Plane and M-plane emulator – test equipment capable of sending and 6 
receiving required messages for all of these protocol planes when the Radio Unit is the device 7 
under test 8 
DL DownLink: data flow towards the radiating antenna 9 
eNB e NodeB (applies to LTE)  <E-UTRAN NodeB / Evolved NodeB> 10 
gNB g NodeB (applies to NR)  <Next Generation NodeB> 11 
M-Plane Management Plane: refers to non-real-time management operations between the O-DU and the O-12 
RU 13 
NETCONF Network Configuration Protocol. For details see: RFC 6241, “Network Configuration Protocol 14 
(NETCONF)”, IETF, June 2011 15 
NMS A Network Management System 16 
O-DU O-RAN Distributed Unit  <O-RAN Distributed Unit: a logical node hosting 17 
PDCP/RLC/MAC/High-PHY layers based on a lower layer functional split.> 18 
O-RU O-RAN Radio Unit  <O-RAN Radio Unit: a logical node hosting Low-PHY layer and RF 19 
processing based on a lower layer functional split.  This is similar to 3GPP’s “TRP” or “RRH” but 20 
more specific in including the Low-PHY layer (FFT/iFFT, PRACH extraction).> 21 
S-Plane Synchronization Plane: refers to traffic between the O-RU or O-DU to a synchronization controller 22 
which is generally an IEEE-1588 Grand Master (however, Grand Master functionality may be 23 
embedded in the O-DU). 24 
TER Test Equipment, O-RU – test equipment used to validate the O-RU 25 
UL UpLink: data flow away from the radiating antenna 26 
U-Plane User Plane: refers to IQ sample data transferred between O-DU and O-RU 27

2 Test Configuration 1 
The conformance tests described in this document require test equipment with specific capabilities to support the testing 2 
of each protocol including the M-Plane, U-Plane, C-Plane and S-Plane. In addition, the tests define a specific 3 
connectivity between the test equipment and the device under test.  This section describes the test equipment 4 
requirements at a high level.  Details are included in each test.   5 
As noted in the introduction in the Scope paragraphs, the initial focus of these conformance tests is the O -RU.  6 
Therefore, the initial test configuration description is focused on the test equipment and configuration required to test 7 
the O-RU.  Future versions of this specification may expand the required test equipment for other O -RAN devices that 8 
are subject to conformance testing.  9 
2.1 Test Configuration for O-RU as the Device Under Test 10 
When testing the O-RU, it is connected to test equipment called Test Equipment O-RU (TER).  The TER is shown in  11 
Figure 2.1-1 below.   TER surrounds the DUT and connects to both the fronthaul interface itself and the radio interface. 12 
At the radio interface the TER collects RF signals from the DUT (downlink) and sends RF signals to the DUT receiver 13 
(uplink).  Thus, the TER is made up of three main components, a CUSM-Plane Emulator (CUSM-E), a signal analyser 14 
and a signal generator as shown in Figure 2.1-1. The RF test interface is as described above and described in TS 38.141-15 
1.  The fronthaul interface is standard Ethernet as described above.  In this case, the DL data flow is evaluated based on 16 
what is received by the signal analyser in the RF domain as radiated by the O-RU, and the UL data flow is evaluated 17 
based on what is emitted by the signal generator in the RF domain and received by the CUSM-E.   18 
When the O-RU is the Device Under Test (DUT), there is Test Equipment, RU (“TER”) that is used to connect to the DUT, run the test 
and evaluate the test result.
fronthaul connection
DUT = O-RU

antenna array(s)

The Test Equipment, RU (“TER”) provides everything needed 
to operate the test, including:
▪ M-Plane commands to collect O-RU capabilities and 
configure the O-RU
▪ Synchronization via G.8275.1 (Mandatory for O-RU)
▪ C-Plane and U-Plane data flow to the O-RU
▪ Collection of RF energy to determine if the O-RU reacted 
correctly to the DL C-Plane and U-Plane data
▪ Radiation of RF energy to be received by the O-RU (note: 
this could be actually radiated, or conveyed through 
multiple RF cabled connections)
▪ Collection of O-RU UL fronthaul data flows and evaluating 
it for correctness based on the supplied RF energy to the 
O-RU antennas or RF connectors

of this description is to show the general capabilities required for all tests on the O-RU as the DUT including U-Plane, 22 
C-Plane and S-Plane tests.  If tests are restricted to only the M-Plane, the required test equipment configuration may be 23 
simplified.   24

3 Conformance Measurements 1 
3.1 M-Plane Measurements 2 
3.1.1 Transport and Handshake Test Scenarios 3 
3.1.1.1 Transport and Handshake in IPv4 Environment (positive case) 4 
 5 
A. Test Description and Applicability 6 
This scenario is MANDATORY. 7 
This scenario validates that the O-RU properly executes the session establishment procedure with VLANs and a 8 
DHCPv4 server.  This test is applicable to IPv4 environments. 9 
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 10 
• 3.1 Management Plane Transport aspects  11 
• 3.2 NETCONF Call Home to O-RU Controller(s) 12 
 13 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 14 
The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are operational, 15 
configured and connected to the O-RU 16 
 17 
C. Test Methodology 18 
a. Initial Conditions 19 
1. The O-RU is powered on and has an ethernet connection to the DHCP-server 20 
2. The configured DHCPv4 server is reachable by the O-RU NETCONF Server through the VLAN 21 
configured for M-Plane. 22 
3. Default SSH credentials (sudo) are used by both the O-RU NETCONF Server and the TER NETCONF 23 
Client 24 
4. IP details for test purposes are pre-defined and fixed (applies to the DHCP server). 25 
 26 
b. Procedure 27 
1. The O-RU NETCONF Server can be preconfigured with no VLAN (known in 802.1Q as native ethernet 28 
or an untagged VLAN), a VLAN ID or may optionally perform a VLAN scan by issuing DHCP Discover 29 
trying to reach the DHCP Server 30 
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server continues the DHCPv4 procedure on the preconfigured VLAN or first 31 
VLAN where the Offer from DHCP Server / Relay is received if the scan method is used 32 
3. O-RU NETCONF Server retrieves IP details and the IP address of the controlling TER NETCONF Client 33 
from the DHCP Server.  Note: RFC 2131 is followed for DHCPv4 34 
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server establishes TCP connection and performs a Call Home procedure towards 35 
the NETCONF Client using the IP details obtained in step 3 36 
5. The TER NETCONF Client establishes a SSH session with the O-RU NETCONF Server.  Proper 37 
credentials are used. 38 
6. The O-RU NETCONF Server accepts the SSH connection establishment from the TER NETCONF Client 39 
7. The TER NETCONF Client and O-RU NETCONF Server exchange capabilities through NETCONF 40 
<hello> messages. 41 
Note: RFC 6241 is followed for NETCONF communication. 42 
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  43 
Test scenario step 7 is performed successfully. 44

Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
16 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
3.1.1.2 Transport and Handshake in IPv4 Environment (negative case) 1 
A. Test Description and Applicability 2 
This scenario is MANDATORY 3 
This scenario validates that the O-RU properly executes the session establishment procedure with VLANs and a 4 
DHCPv4 server.  This test is applicable to IPv4 environments.  Two negative flows are included in this test: 5 
• The TER NETCONF Client does not trigger a SSH session establishment in reaction to Call Home 6 
initiated by THE O-RU NETCONF Server. 7 
• The TER NETCONF Client uses improper credentials when trying to establish a SSH session with the O-8 
RU NETCONF Server. 9 
 10 
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 11 
• 3.1 Management Plane Transport aspects 12 
• 3.2 NETCONF Call Home to O-RU Controller(s) 13 
 14 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 15 
The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are operational, 16 
configured and connected to the O-RU. 17 
 18 
C. Test Methodology 19 
a. Initial Conditions 20 
a. O-RU is powered on and has an ethernet connection to the DHCP-server 21 
b. Configured DHCPv4 server is reachable for O-RU NETCONF Server through the VLAN configured for 22 
M-Plane. 23 
c. Default SSH credentials (sudo) are used by both O-RU NETCONF Server and NETCONF Client 24 
d. IP details for test purposes are pre-defined and fixed (applies to DHCP server). 25 
e. Procedure 26 
i. Flow 1 27 
1. The O-RU NETCONF Server can be preconfigured with no VLAN (known in 802.1Q as native 28 
ethernet or an untagged VLAN), a VLAN ID or may optionally perform a VLAN scan by issuing a 29 
DHCP Discover trying to reach DHCP Server 30 
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server continues the DHCPv4 procedure on the preconfigured VLAN or first 31 
VLAN where the Offer from the DHCP Server / Relay is received if the scan method is used 32 
3. The O-RU NETCONF Server retrieves IP details and the IP address of controlling TER NETCONF 33 
Client from the DHCP Server.  Note: RFC 2131 is followed for DHCPv4 34 
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server establishes TCP connection and performs Call Home procedure with 35 
the TER NETCONF Client using IP details obtained in step 3 36 
5. The TER NETCONF Client does not initiate the SSH session establishment procedure. 37 
6. The O-RU NETCONF Server periodically repeats the Call Home towards TER NETCONF Client.  38 
 39 
ii. Flow 2 40 
1. The O-RU NETCONF Server can be preconfigured with a VLAN ID or may optionally perform a 41 
VLAN scan by issuing a DHCP Discover trying to reach the DHCP Server 42 
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server continues the DHCPv4 procedure on the preconfigured VLAN or first 43 
VLAN where the Offer from the DHCP Server / Relay is received if the scan method is used 44 
3. The O-RU NETCONF Server retrieves IP details and the IP address of the controlling TER 45 
NETCONF Client from DHCP Server.  Note: RFC 2131 is followed for DHCPv4  46 
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server establishes a TCP connection and performs the Call Home procedure 47 
with the TER NETCONF Client using IP details obtained in step 3 48 
5. The TER NETCONF Client initiates the SSH session establishment procedure with improper 49 
credentials. 50 
6. Due to the incorrect SSH credentials, the O-RU NETCONF Server rejects the SSH connection 51 
establishment from the TER NETCONF Client. 52 
7. The O-RU NETCONF Server starts periodic Call Home procedure towards the TER NETCONF 53 
Client. 54 
 55 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
17 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  1 
1. Flow 1: Scenario reaches step 6.  The O-RU NETCONF Server falls into Call Home procedure loop. 2 
2. Flow 2: Scenario reaches step 7.  The O-RU NETCONF Server falls into Call Home procedure loop. 3

6. Due to the incorrect SSH credentials, the O-RU NETCONF Server rejects the SSH connection 54 
establishment from the TER NETCONF Client. 55 
7. The O-RU NETCONF Server starts periodic Call Home procedure to the TER NETCONF Client. 56

to the O-RU NETCONF Server. 15

C. Test Methodology 1 
a. Initial Conditions 2 
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.1.1 or 3.1.1.3for IPv4 and IPv6 respectively is successfully 3 
completed. 4 
 5 
b. Procedure 6 
1. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><get><filter> towards NETCONF Server.  The <filter> 7 
argument contains a regular expression that the O-RU NETCONF Server shall apply as a filter. For 8 
example, a filter that filters all low-level-rx-endpoints:  9 
  <rpc message-id="101" xmlns="urn:o-ran:uplane-conf:1.0" > 10 
      <get> 11 
          <source>running</source> 12 
          <filter type = ”subtree”> 13 
              <top xmlns="urn:o-ran:uplane-conf:1.0/”> 14 
                  <user-plane-configuration> 15 
                      <low-level-rx-endpoints> 16 
                      </low-level-rx-endpoints> 17 
                  </user-plane-configuration> 18 
              </top> 19 
          </filter> 20 
      </get> 21 
   </rpc> 22 
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-reply><data> where <data> contains details for objects 23 
as conforming to the <filter> (as per the above example filter: all low-level-rx-endpoints) 24 
 25 
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 26 
Test step 2 is performed successfully. 27

3.1.6 O-RU Software Update 14 
3.1.6.1 O-RU Software Update and Install (positive case) 15 
A. Test Description and Applicability 16 
This scenario is MANDATORY 17 
This test validates that the O-RU can successfully perform a software download and software install procedure.  18 
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 19 
• 5. Software Management 20 
 21 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 22 
The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are operational, 23 
configured and connected to the O-RU. 24 
C. Test Methodology 25 
a. Initial Conditions 26 
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 27 
2. A correct and internally consistent SW package is available for test purposes.  28 
3. The O-RU provides at least one slot available for SW update procedure.  The status of this slot is assumed 29 
to be {active = False, running = False, access = READ-WRITE} 30 
4. A sFTP server is available with an account for the SW update procedure on the TER  31 
 32 
b. Procedure 33 
1. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><software-download>.  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds 34 
with <rpc-reply><software-download> 35 
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server performs a software download procedure.  When the download is 36 
completed, the O-RU NETCONF Server sends <notification><download-event> with status 37 
COMPLETED to TER NETCONF Client 38 
3. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><software-install> informing the O-RU NETCONF Client 39 
about the desired slot for installation.  This slot must have the attributes active = FALSE, running = 40 
FALSE, access = READ-WRITE.  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-reply><software-41 
install> with status STARTED. 42 
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server examines the downloaded software.  The files are error free by design in 43 
this test.  The O-RU NETCONF Server installs the new software files to the desired slot.  44 
5. The O-RU NETCONF Server sends <notification><install-event><status> to the TER NETCONF Client. 45 
Field <status> contains the value COMPLETED to indicate the successful installation of software to the 46 
desired slot. 47 
 48 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
25 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 1 
1. Test step 5 completed with notification that indicates successful installation of  the downloaded software. 2 
2. Status of SW slot used for SW installation is set to VALID.  Other parameters of software slot shall not be 3 
changed. 4 
 5 
3.1.6.2 O-RU Software Update (negative case) 6 
A. Test Description and Applicability 7 
This scenario is MANDATORY. 8 
This scenario corresponds the following chapters in [3]: 9 
• 5. Software Management 10 
 11 
B. Test Purpose 12 
This test validates that the O-RU can successfully perform a software download procedure.  One or more files are 13 
intentionally corrupted to make sure that the O-RU is able to recognize an invalid software update file and protect 14 
itself from installing this file.  15 
C. Test Methodology 16 
a. Initial Conditions 17 
The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 18 
A modified software package is available for test purposes (proper content of manifest.xml, but fake /invalid 19 
content of software files) 20 
The O-RU provides at least one slot available for the software update procedure (status != INVALID, active = 21 
False, running = False, access = READ-WRITE) 22 
A sFTP server is available with an account dedicated for the software update procedure 23 
b. Procedure 24 
1. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><software-download>.  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds 25 
with <rpc-reply><software-download> 26 
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server performs the software download procedure.  When the download is 27 
complete, the O-RU NETCONF Server sends <notification><download-event> with status COMPLETED 28 
to the TER NETCONF Client 29 
3. The TER NETCONF Client triggers <rpc><software-install> informing the O-RU NETCONF Server 30 
about desired slot the software shall be installed to.  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-31 
reply><software-install> with status STARTED. 32 
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server determines that the software file is invalid and sends <notification><install-33 
event><status> to the TER NETCONF Client.  The Field <status> is correctly updated with one of the 34 
following status: FILE_ERROR or INTEGRITY_ERROR. 35 
 36 
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 37 
1. Test step 4 completed a described. 38 
2. Status of SW slot used for SW installation is set to INVALID.  Other parameters of software slot shall not be 39 
changed. 40 
 41

software just activated.  31

 22 
b. Procedure 23

already present and passwords these three accounts using o-ran-user.mgmt.yang 26

4. The O-RU NETCONF Server confirms the operations for the above transactions 29

user accounts and mappings are validated. 31

3.1.9  External Input / Output Ports 26 
3.1.9.1 External Input Port State Detection 27 
A. Test Description and Applicability 28 
This scenario is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. The test is applicable only for O-RUs supporting logical input 29 
ports. 30 
This test validates proper handling of logical input ports. 31 
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 32 
• 11.4.1 External Input 33 
 34 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 35 
• The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are 36 
operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 37 
• Supplementary circuitry is required to force a change of logical state of input lines belonging to an input port. 38 
It is assumed that logical input ports are internally pulled to logical high state by O -RU, therefore 39 
supplementary circuitry shall only allow to change the input port to a logical low. To determine a physical 40 
input line for this test, one shall read the customer documentation applicable for the O-RU being tested. 41 
 42 
C. Test Methodology 43 
a. Initial Conditions 44 
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 45 
 46 
b. Procedure 47 
1. The External Input Ports are left in their normal, default stated.  For the purposes of this test, these input 48 
ports are assumed to be a logical high.  49 
2. The TER NETCONF Client retrieves state of chosen input port by issuing <rpc><get><filter 50 
type="subtree"><external-io xml...><input><port-in></port-in></input></external-51 
io></filter></get></rpc> 52 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
31 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
3. The O-RU NETCONF Server provides the state of every line-in belonging to the input port under test to 1 
the TER NETCONF Client. For all input lines, the state is TRUE, indicating open circuit (no shortage to 2 
ground is detected by input lines) 3 
4. The TER supplementary circuitry randomly shorts one or more input lines to the ground. Changes shall 4 
occur with a periodicity greater than 30 seconds. 5 
5. For every change the O-RU NETCONF Server sends notification <external-input-change> to the TER 6 
NETCONF Client.   The notification contains updated states of input lines belonging to the port under test. 7 
A state FALSE indicates shortage to ground detected by particular input line.  8 
6. This test scenario is looped to step 4 for a total of 10 iterations 9 
 10 
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 11 
Step 5 is correctly validated for each iteration of the test.  12

3.1.9.2 External Output Port State Control 14 
A. Test Description and Applicability 15 
This scenario is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. The test is applicable only for O-RUs supporting logical output 16 
ports. 17 
This test validates proper handling of logical output ports. 18 
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 19 
• 11.4.2 External Output 20 
 21 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 22 
• The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are 23 
operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 24 
• Supplementary circuitry is required to measure voltage of an output port signal.  To determine the mapping of 25 
physical output lines to ports, one shall read customer documentation for the O-RU being tested.  The 26 
definition of voltage levels served by output lines of output ports and the maximum allowed current sourced by 27 
single an output line shall be validated against the TER capabilities. 28 
 29 
C. Test Methodology 30 
a. Initial Conditions 31 
1. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 32 
 33 
b. Procedure 34 
1. The TER NETCONF Client issues :<rpc><edit-config> to the O-RU NETCONF Server requesting all 35 
output lines belonging to output port to be set to FALSE. 36 
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server sets logical LOW state to output lines corresponding to step 1 and responds 37 
to TER NETCONF Client with <rpc-reply> 38 
3. The TER supplementary circuitry shows that all output lines of the target output port are set to logical 39 
LOW state. 40 
4. The TER NETCONF Client issues :<rpc><edit-config> towards NETCONF Server requesting a random 41 
change of states of output lines belonging to target output port.  Changes shall occur with a periodicity 42 
greater than 30 seconds. 43 
5. The O-RU NETCONF Server sets the requested states of output lines for the states defined by step 4 and 44 
responds to NETCONF Client with <rpc-reply>.  The TER supplementary circuitry validates the change. 45 
6. This test scenario is looped to step 4 for a total of 10 iterations 46 
 47 
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 48 
Step 5 is correctly validated for each iteration of the test.  49

3.1.11 ALD Communications 10 
3.1.11.1 ALD Communications Test 11 
A. Test Description and Applicability 12 
This scenario is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY for a O-RU equipped with a RET port (regardless of whether 13 
this is a raw RS-485 port or OOK modem coupled internally to antenna connector (s)).  This scenario shall be 14 
performed against each ALD port exposed by the O-RU. 15 
The purpose of the test is to validate the ALD communications protocol and operation of the O -RU. The following 16 
functions are validated in this test. 17 
• Proper transmission of the content if RPC <ald-communication> towards desired ALD port 18 
• Proper calculation of FCS 19 
• Proper application of basic transparency to content to be transmitted 20 
• Proper addition of start / stop flags 21 
• Proper reception of payload injected to ALD port 22 
• Proper removal of start / stop flags 23 
• Proper application of basic transparency to content received from ALD port 24 
• Proper validation of FCS in data received from ALD port. 25 
 26 
This scenario corresponds to the following chapters in [3]: 27 
• 11.3 Operational aspects of Antenna Line Devices 28 
 29 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 30 
• The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are 31 
operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 32 
• It is assumed, that O-RU being a subject of this conformance test scenario is proven to be complia nt to the 33 
following specifications: 34 
1. ISO/IEC 13239:2002 “High-level data link control (HDLC) procedures” 35 
2. 3GPP TS 25.460 “UTRAN Iuant Interface: General aspects and principles” 36 
3. 3GPP TS 25.461 ”UTRAN Iuant Interface: Layer 1” 37 
4. 3GPP TS 25.462 ”UTRAN Iuant Interface: Signalling Transport” 38 
5. 3GPP TS 25.466 “UTRAN Iuant Interface: Application Part” 39 
• The O-RU uses a 9.6 kbps data rate on its ALD port(s) for transmission and reception, regardless of connector 40 
supported by particular ALD port. 41 
 42 
 43 
C. Test Methodology 44 
As O-RU does not verify correctness of the payload that is exchanged between NETCONF Client and ALD (except 45 
FCS for traffic coming from ALD) - any payload can be used in test vector, under condition, that test vectors are 46 
compliant to referenced above set of specification documents (e.g. length is not smaller than minimum size of real 47 
message). 48 
RS-485 sniffer / injector is needed for this test. Such a device shall be connected either to O-RU’s RS-485 port or 49 
to RS-485 port of Smart BiasT connected to O-RU with coaxial cable (depending on O-RU construction) 50 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
34 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
Unless not specified otherwise – RS-485 sniffer / injector shall be connected to ALD port corresponding to record 1 
“port-id” used in RPC <ald-communication>. 2 
In case O-RU exposes ALD port as antenna port, test environment should utilize Smart BiasT for conversion 3 
between OOK modulation at antenna port and RS-485 signaling that RS-485 sniffer / injector can handle. DC 4 
voltage for Smart BiasT device shall be provided by O-RU through antenna feeder. 5 
If not specified otherwise, for test purposes RS-485 sniffer / injector is connected to ALD port which will be 6 
addressed in RPC <ald-communication> within the scenario. 7 
As this test is intended to verify O-RU functions and there will be no real ALD connected – compliance to the 8 
required HDLC message structure is required, whilst the AISG payload can be artificial (unless otherwise specified 9 
in test case). The O-RU does not verify if messaging is correct, hence, for test simplicity and ease of test result 10 
verification, artificial test vectors can be used. 11 
a. Initial Conditions 12 
2. The test procedure described in section 3.1.4.1 is successfully completed. 13 
 14 
a. Procedure 15 
i. Test Case 1: Transmission towards ALD (positive scenario) 16 
Scope: CRC calculation, transparency algorithm application, start / stop flag addition, datagram 17 
transmission using desired ALD port  18 
1) NETCONF Client sends regular RPC <ald-communication> message containing bytes 0x7D and 19 
0x7E in “ald-req-msg” record. 20 
2) O-RU calculates FCS, adds it to datagram provided in record “ald-req-msg”, applies basic 21 
transparency (replaces every occurrence of byte “0x7E” with two bytes “0x7D 0x5E”, respectively, 22 
replace byte “0x7D” with two bytes “0x7D 0x5D”) and add start/stop flags 0x 7E. 23 
3) O-RU sends payload calculated in step 2 through ALD port mentioned in record “port -id” of RPC. 24 
4) RS-485 sniffer / injector receives payload sent by O-RU. Received payload is subject of analysis for 25 
scenario success / failure classification 26 
 27 
ii. Test Case 1 Test Requirement (expected result) 28 
Content received by RS-485 listener / injector is compared with content of RPC <ald-communication>. 29 
a) payload shall be sent by desired ALD port of O-RU 30 
b) FCS shall be properly calculated 31 
c) basic transparency shall be properly applied 32 
d) start / stop flags shall be added to payload that has been received by RS-485 sniffer / injector 33 
Test scenario is considered as completed with success in case all mentioned above conditions are satisfied. 34 
Any deviation means test scenario is failed. 35 
 36 
iii. Test Case 2: Reception from ALD (positive case) 37 
Scope: datagram reception, start / stop flag detection and removal, transparency algorithm applications, 38 
CRC verification  39 
Note: Test case 2 shall be performed just after Test case 1 so that content injected by RS-485 sniffer / 40 
injector is considered by O-RU as ALD’s response to message sent towards ALD in Test case 1. Timing 41 
between Test case 1 and Test case 2 shall follow 3GPP specifications mentioned above.  42 
1) RS485 sniffer / injector sends properly formatted (start / stop flags, FCS and min / max payload size) 43 
message containing strings “0x7D 0x5E” and “0x7D 0x5D” towards O-RU’s ALD port used in Test 44 
case 1. 45 
2) O-RU receives the content. 46 
3) O-RU removes start / stop flags, performs basic transparency (replaces “0x7D 0x5E” with “0x7E” 47 
and “0x7D 0x5D” with “0x7D”), makes sure if FCS is correct according content of datagram.  48 
4) O-RU sends “ald-resp-msg” towards NETCONF Client. 49 
 50 
iv. Test Case 2 Requirement (expected result) 51 
Content received by NETCONF Client is compared with content injected by RS-485 sniffer / injector. 52

a) record “ald-port” shall indicate proper O-RU’s ALD port as source of the payload 1 
b) basic transparency is properly applied 2 
b) counter of received octets is properly incremented 3 
d) counters of frames with wrong FCS (CRC) and frames without stop flags are not incremented  4

v. Test Case 3: Reception from ALD (negative case – wrong FCS) 7

2) O-RU receives the content. 15 
3) O-RU removes start / stop flags, performs basic transparency (replaces “0x7D 0x5E” with “0x7E” and 16

4) O-RU sends “ald-resp-msg” towards NETCONF Client. 18

b) record “ald-resp-msg” is empty 23 
b) counter of received octets and counter of frames without stop flags are not incremented  24 
d) counters of frames with wrong FCS (CRC) is incremented 25 
Test scenario is considered as completed with success in case all mentioned above conditions are satisfied. 26 
Any deviation means test scenario is failed. 27 
 28 
vii. Test Case 4: Reception from ALD (negative case – no stop flag) 29 
Scope: datagram reception, start / stop flag detection 30 
Note: Test case 4 shall be performed just after Test case 1 so that content injected by RS-485 sniffer / 31 
injector is considered by O-RU as ALD’s response to message sent towards ALD in Test case 1. Timing 32 
between Test case 1 and Test case 4 shall follow 3GPP specifications mentioned above.  33 
1) RS-485 sniffer / injector sends message not terminated by stop flag “0x7E” towards O -RU’s ALD port 34 
used in Test case 1. 35 
2) O-RU receives the content. 36 
3) O-RU reaches the end of reception window without receiving stop flag that would terminate the 37 
datagram. 38 
4) O-RU sends “ald-resp-msg” towards NETCONF Client. 39

• The minimum functions of the TER described in section 2.1 that support validation of the M-Plane are 10 
operational, configured and connected to the O-RU. 11 
• Supplementary circuitry is required to measure voltage of an output port signal.  To determine the mapping of 12 
physical output lines to ports, one shall read customer documentation for the O-RU being tested.  The 13

single an output line shall be validated against the TER capabilities. 15

 20 
b. Procedure 21 
1. The TER NETCONF Client sends <rpc><start-troubleshooting-logs> to the O-RU NETCONF Server.  22 
The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-reply>< troubleshooting-status-grouping >. 23 
2. The O-RU NETCONF Server starts generating one or more file(s) containing troubleshooting logs.  When 24 
the generation of the log file(s) are completed, the O-RU NETCONF Server sends 25 
<notification><troubleshooting-log-generated> with a list of one or more log file names to the TER 26 
NETCONF Server.  27 
NOTE: It is assumed that the generated log file(s) contains troubleshooting logs related to alarm 17 28 
measured in 3.1.5.2 but the content and format are not specified. 29 
3. The TER NETCONF Client sends  <rpc><file-upload>log-file-name</file-upload></rpc> to the O-RU 30 
NETCONF Server to start uploading the log file(s).  The O-RU NETCONF Server responds with <rpc-31 
reply><file-upload> with status SUCCESS.  32 
4. The O-RU NETCONF Server uploads the log file(s) to NETCONF Client by sFTP. When file upload is 33 
completed, the O-RU NETCONF Server sends <notification><upload-notification> with status 34 
SUCCESS. 35 
 36 
D. Test Requirement (expected result) 37 
Test step 4 is performed successfully. 38 
NOTE: The O-RU vendor may check the contents of the uploaded log file in detail for the reported alarm 17, 39 
but as noted, the content and format of troubleshooting logs are not defined. 40

3.2 UC-Plane Measurements 2 
3.2.1 UC-Plane Standard Test Definitions 3 
The following sections describe test scenarios for equipment implementing the U -Plane and C-Plane O-RAN option 4 
7.2x protocols.    5 
The initial focus of this conformance test document is validation of the O-RU as the device under test (DUT).  Future 6 
versions of this specification may address conformance tests with other devices as the DUT.  7 
3.2.1.1 UC-Plane Measurements, O-RU TEST SCENARIO 8 
In these sets of tests, the Device Under Test (DUT) is the O-RU.   9 
This document describes conformance tests for 4 scenarios: 10 
1. Conducted FDD tests for FR1 radios 11 
2. Non-conducted (OTA) FDD tests for FR1 radios 12 
3. Conducted TDD tests for FR1 radios 13 
4. Non-conducted tests for TDD FR1 and FR2 radios 14 
 15 
The O-RU must only be tested for the scenarios that apply to the O-RU capabilities. The fact that there are 4 scenarios 16 
defined does not imply that every O-RU must be tested for all scenarios in order to be O-RAN compliant and 17 
consequently the O-RU does not have to support all the capabilities required to test all 4 scenarios (i.e. supp ort of FR1, 18 
FR2, TDD, FDD, conducted and non-conducted). In other words, depending on whether the O-RU supports capabilities 19 
such as FDD, TDD, FR1 and or FR2, the corresponding scenarios that match the O -RU capabilities will apply only. For 20 
example, an O-RU that does not have or cannot provide access to antenna ports (or TAB connectors), supports TDD 21 
and operates at FR2 bands, the corresponding scenario that the O-RU will need to be tested to be O-RAN conformance 22 
is scenario #4 only. Another example, for an O-RU that supports FDD, operates at FR1 bands and has or can provide 23 
access to antenna ports (or TAB connectors), scenario #1 or #2 can apply but only one of the two possible scenarios will 24 
be selected to test the O-RU for O-RAN conformance.  The current release of this conformance test specification only 25 
defines conformance test procedures for scenario #1. Any O-RU under test where scenario #1 applies must pass the 26 
conformance test following the procedures defined in scenario #1. On the other hand, if the O-RU under test can only 27 
be tested for conformance via the currently undefined scenarios (#2, #3 or #4 apply to this O-RU and no procedures are 28 
defined at the time of the test), the result of the O-RAN CU-plane conformance test for this O-RU should be 29 
“Inconclusive” or “Not Applicable”. 30 
 31 
For scenario #1 and #3 above the RF test setup is as described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE].  For 32 
scenarios #2 and #4 the RF test setup is as described in TS 38.141-2. Note that O-RAN conformance testing is expected 33 
to be “off-line” and not to be run while an O-DU and/or O-RU is operating and serving actual users.  The O-RU 34 
manufacturer must also make available the same declarations described in 3GPP TS 38.141 -1[NR] and TS 36.141 35 
[LTE] Section 4.6.  This will determine the radio’s support for multi -carrier operation (e.g., IF multi-carrier operation is 36 
supported on different connectors) 37 
Since the purpose of this document is to test O-RAN Fronthaul conformance and not to duplicate 3GPP RF tests only 38 
selected parts of TS 38.141[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE] will be used for RF testing.  These selected test features are only 39 
necessary to test whether the O-RU correctly interpreted and generated the O-RAN C-Plane and U-Plane messages 40 
correctly. There will also be some additions to the test waveforms used in TS 38.141[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE] to fully 41 
exercise the features of the O-RAN Fronthaul protocol.  These selected parts and additions are summarized below: 42 
3.2.1.1.1 For scenario #1 (Conducted FDD tests for FR1 radios) 43 
• For downlink tests for type 1-C radios (radios with antenna port connectors and passive antennas) the test 44 
configuration described in TS 38.141 D.1.1 will be used.  Only a single antenna port will be used unless the 45 
test explicitly requires more than one port and the radio supports more than one port.  RF test equipment will 46

be connected at the point described in TS 38.141-1 section 4.2.1. Note that an antenna port is an electrical 1 
conducting port that is connected to an array element. 2 
• For uplink tests for type 1-C radios (radios with antenna port connectors and passive antennas) the test 3 
configuration described in TS 38.141 D.2.1 will be used.  Only a single antenna port will be used unless the 4 
test explicitly requires more than one port and the radio supports more than one port.  RF test equipment will 5 
be connected at the point described in TS 38.141-1 section 4.2.1. Note that an antenna port is an electrical 6 
conducting port that is connected to an array element. 7 
• For downlink tests for type 1-H radios (radios with TAB connectors and active antenna systems) the test 8 
configuration described in TS 38.141 D.3.1 will be used for conduct ed tests.  Only a single TAB connector will 9 
be used unless the test explicitly requires more than one connector.  RF test equipment will be connected at the 10 
point described in TS 38.141-1 section 4.2.2. Note that a transceiver array boundary (TAB) connector is an 11 
electrical conducting port that is connected to an array element via a radio distribution network (RDN).  12 
• For uplink tests for type 1-H radios (radios with TAB connectors and active antenna systems) the test 13 
configuration described in TS 38.141 D.4.1 will be used for conducted tests.  Only a single TAB connector will 14 
be used unless the test explicitly requires more than one connector.  RF test equipment will be connected at the 15 
point described in TS 38.141-1 section 4.2.2. Note that a transceiver array boundary (TAB) connector is an 16 
electrical conducting port that is connected to an array element via a radio distribution network (RDN).  17 
• The basic downlink test will start with the Test model described in NR-FR1-TM1.1 and E-TM1.1.  Subsequent 18 
tests will adapt this model to test additional features of the O-RAN interface (e.g., Modifying the payload data, 19 
blanking some symbols, etc.).  Note this test model describes the IQ data contained in the O-RAN packets not 20 
the O-RAN specific parameters.  This test model will also be augmented with the following O-RAN specific 21 
parameters: 22 
Includes “stock” eAxC values as configured via M-Plane: 23 
• DU_Port_ID: two bits, nominal value 00b 24 
• BandSector: nominal 6 bits, nominal value 000000b 25 
• CC_ID: nominal 4 bits, nominal value 0000b (most tests invoke only one component carrier) 26 
• RU_port_ID: 4 bits, nominal values 0000b through 0011b or to whatever max value needed for a 27 
specific test 28 
• If the radio manufacturer declares support for multi-carrier a different eAxC will be assigned for each carrier. 29 
Note that most tests described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE]  require testing at the bottom, 30 
middle and top of the supported bands of the radio.  This specification r elaxes that requirement because the 31 
purpose is to test the fronthaul compliance and not the radio performance. 32 
• Compression: Static 16-bit fixed point IQ bitwidth in both DL and UL 33 
• Beamforming: no beamforming (beamId = 0x0000), assumed to mean boresight radiation (normal to the 34 
antenna surface) at some undetermined beamwidth (recall that beam weight magnitudes must be equal to 35 
unity) 36 
• Transport: L2 Ethernet, eCPRI with no fragmentation and no QOS 37 
• Delay Parameters: The test will be executed with a direct fiber connection to the O-RU therefore T12_min = 38 
T12_max = 0.  Similarly, T34_min = T34_max = 0. 39 
The radio will report its supported values for: 40 
o T2a_min/max_up = T1a_min/max_up (fixed, zero network delay) 41 
o Ta3_min/max_up = Ta4_min_max_up (fixed, zero network delay) 42 
o T2a_min/max_cp_ul = T1a_min/max_cp_ul (fixed, zero network delay) 43 
o Tcp_adv_dl 44 
      These parameters will be used to calculate the delay windows needed for the delay management tests 45 
below. 46 
• Uplink tests will start with the basic 3GPP test signal for Fixed Reference Channels for receiver sensitivity and 47 
in-channel selectivity as described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE].  All O-RAN specific 48 
parameters will be the same as described above for downlink testing.  As with downlink testing subsequent 49 
tests will build on this basic waveform modifying parameters as needed to exercise O-RAN specific features. 50 
• Uplink tests will be conducted using power levels at least 30dB higher than the power levels used to test 3GPP 51 
Receiver sensitivity described in 3GPP TS 38.141-1 Table 7.2.5-1[NR] and TS 36.141 [LTE]. This is to ensure 52 
a clear signal is received by the O-RU so it can be accurately decoded and demodulated to ensure the correct 53 
data was received by the O-DU as was sent by the signal source.  Again, the purpose of these tests is to ensure 54 
correct operation of the O-RAN fronthaul not to test receiver sensitivity. 55

3.2.1.1.5 Test Configuration for the UC-Plane 7 
The TER shown in Figure 2.1-1 provides M-Plane and S-Plane commands and sequences to correctly set up the O-RU 8 
for testing using the fronthaul connection – meaning a criterion and prerequisite for executing all UC-Plane tests is 9 
proper operation of the O-RU’s synchronization and M-Plane capabilities.  The TER provides the specific C-Plane and 10 
U-Plane data flows and collects data from the radiated energy from the O-RU and evaluates based on the collected RF 11 
energy whether the O-RU correctly received and interpreted the fronthaul DL data flow.  For many tests a single RF 12 
detector is satisfactory to detect the radiated signal but for beamforming tests an RF pattern must be measured to 13 
validate the correct beam is being generated according to the C-Plane commands and U-Plane data flowing across the 14 
fronthaul interface. 15 
In addition, the TER generates RF energy using the signal generator and feeds it to the O -RU’s antennas (or antenna 16 
connectors) which is expected to be used by the O-RU, in conjunction with the C-Plane UL commands sent by the TER 17 
over the fronthaul connection, to generate UL data flows on the fronthaul connection which are received and evaluated 18 
by the TER.  For all tests a single RF emitter is satisfactory to generate the radiated signal, even beamforming tests 19 
wherein the received power level will validate that the beam main lobe was correctly specified across the fronthaul 20 
interface. 21 
3GPP-specified tests will be used here to simplify the testing, because such tests will need to be supported by the O -RU 22 
anyway for 3GPP conformance testing.  The specific test cases identify where this is possible and where changes must 23 
be made to adequately test O-RAN features. 24 
Note that when testing the O-RU for fronthaul interface conformance, much more than the fronthaul interface is being 25 
tested, indeed the entire O-RU is under test, including digital and analog processing having nothing to do with the 26 
fronthaul interface.  Therefore a “passed” test can be interpreted with some confidence a s indicating a properly 27 
operating fronthaul interface, but a “failed” test may indicate a problem with the fronthaul interface or with some other 28 
operation within the O-RU therefore failed tests may require some troubleshooting.  While 3GPP TS 38.141-1[NR] and 29 
TS 36.141 [LTE] describes the basic waveform used in these tests it does not describe how the various channels should 30 
be put into O-RAN sections.  The 3GPP TS 38.141-1 NR-FR1-TM1.1[NR]and TS 36.141 [LTE] signal is tightly 31 
packed with data.  All tests will divide that data into “stock” data sections using the sections described below.   To 32 
expedite the definition and creation of the tests, a set of standard test environments and patterns is defined in this 33 
section.  This includes a “stock” arrangement of data sections in DL (same is used for UL) which can be used regardless 34 
of the specific bandwidth and SCS used in the test.  Specifically, there are “stock” 1-symbol, 2-symbol, and 3-symbol 35 
data section sets that shall be cited in test definitions (numbered “A” through “F”) that will support various test cases.  36 
The test cases are expected to specify the data section definition of a test slot and all slots are expected to follow the 37 
same data section definition unless a test specifically states otherwise.  In many cases only some symbols within a slot 38 
will be subject to testing; the remaining symbols are expected to remain undefined for the test and may have data 39 
sections defined according to the normal operation of the O-DU (e.g. set to carry synch or reference signals consistent 40 
with LTE or NR).  In cases where a specific type of data section cannot  be supported by the DUT, then that data section 41 
is omitted in the symbol(s) and the corresponding U-Plane data shall be set to zero in DL (and arranged to have no RF 42 
power in UL).  Figure 3.2.1.1-1 shows the “stock” data section definition. 43

E: 2 symbol 2 sections : tests multi-symbol section, symIncbit
F: 3 symbols many sections : tests data gaps, reMask, multi-symbol sections

Figure 3.2.1.1-1 Stock Data Section Definition for both DL and UL 2 
 3 
There is also “stock” U-Plane data that is PN9 data, representing user data prior to modulation, as specified within 4 
3GPP [CCITT Recommendation O.151 (10/92): https://www.itu.int/rec/T-REC-O.151-199210-I/en] which is assumed 5 
to start at a frame boundary and be identical in all frames in both DL and UL, unless a specific test states differently.  6 
The PN sequence is expected to be running for the duration of the frame for whatever is the bandwidth and  SCS (this is 7 
different from how the data sections are handled, wherein the data sections are truncated based on the number of PRBs 8 
per symbol).  However, in many cases only some symbols within a frame will be actually subject to testing (as defined 9 
by the specific tests) so will contain the test PN sequence data; the remaining symbols are expected to remain undefined 10 
for the test and may contain data according to the normal operation of the O -DU (e.g. set to carry synch or reference 11 
signals consistent with LTE or NR).  Note that the PN sequence initial value is provided by a seed which may be 12 
included as a Test Command parameter. If the parameter is omitted to PN sequence will use a “seed” value of all ones.  13 
For all tests, the test definition shall define the specific slots and symbols subject to test (carrying the “stock” C-Plane 14 
data section definition and the “stock” U-Plane data) with the remaining slots and symbols undefined but possibly 15 
carrying normal 3GPP synch and control data and empty user data.  All slots and symbols subject to test are identical in 16 
each frame, so tests do not have to wait for a specific frame number and are not expected to reset or otherwise perturb 17 
the normal frame number sequence.  This is intended to allow the test to disrupt normal O-DU and O-RU operation as 18 
little as possible. If there is a specific need to validate the construction of a specific frame or slot of data, a test may 19 
elect to zero the test data and leave undefined the data sections for all except one slot or frame of data; where this is 20 
necessary it will be described in the specific test definition, but this is expected to be an exceptional case.  21 
3.2.1.1.6 Generic Steps for Test Execution, O-RU TEST SCENARIO 22 
The following are the generic test steps used when testing the O-RU, although specific tests may deviate from this 23 
general procedure: 24 
1) Configure the Test Equipment, O-RU (TER) for test execution, which may include defining the specific test to 25 
execute. This may also include using a scripting language for describing the test. 26 
2) Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 27 
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. 28 
3) Send appropriate C-Plane and U-Plane DL data flows and collect the O-RU radiated energy (or collect from 29 
antenna connectors) using RF detection equipment. 30 
4) Evaluate the RF energy pattern from the O-RU to determine if the O-RU correctly received and interpreted the 31 
fronthaul C-Plane and U-Plane data flows.  In some cases it also includes decoding and demodulating the RF 32 
signal to ensure all UC-Plane messages were interpreted correctly. 33 
5) Send appropriate C-Plane messages to define the desired UL U-Plane flow, at the same time cause the RF 34 
signal generator to radiate (or feed into antenna connectors) the appropriate RF energy pattern  for the test.  35 
This also means meeting the appropriate timing windows to allow the O-RU to decode and process the C-Plane 36 
messages before the signal generator starts sending RF. 37 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
44 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
6) Collect the O-RU UL data flows on the fronthaul interface and evaluate for correctness; this will generally be 1 
U-Plane data only but in limited cases (LAA) may include UL C-Plane messages too. 2

3.2.1.2 UC-Plane Measurements, O-DU Test Scenario 4

3.2.2 Minimum Capabilities of the TER for U-Plane and C-Plane Tests 6 
Since many features of the O-RAN protocol rely on the O-DU instructing the O-RU to put data in specific resource 7 
blocks using a specific compression method it is imperative that the test equipment support features that allow 8 
comparing data on the fronthaul side with data on the RF side of the radio. 9 
3.2.2.1 Signal Analyzer 10 
• Must have the capability of decoding and demodulating an RF signal either received over the air or on  a 11 
conducted interface.  This data must be made available for comparison with data sent on the fronthaul 12 
interface. 13 
• Must be able to determine the Phase and amplitude of any signal for beamforming tests. 14 
• Obviously must support the frequency range of the radio being tested. 15 
3.2.2.2 Signal Generator 16 
• Must provide software capable of building a correct 5G or LTE waveform. 17 
• Should have the ability to automatically build 3GPP compliant test waveforms and should provide a 18 
mechanism for editing the parameters of that waveform. 19 
• Must be able to be synchronized with the O-DU emulator to ensure proper timing of uplink C-Plane and U-20 
Plane messages 21 
3.2.2.3 CUSM-ECUSM-Plane Emulator (CUSM-E) 22 
• Must be able to extract IQ data from uplink U-Plane messages and demodulate and decode the data to ensure it 23 
is the same as what was commanded in the uplink C-Plane messages. 24 
• Must have the ability to synchronize with the RF signal source. 25 
• Should have the ability to perform as a PTP Master or slave depending on the synchronization configuration 26 
the radio supports. 27 
• Must have the ability to accept frequency domain IQ and encapsulate it according to user input on the correct 28 
sections. 29 
 30 
3.2.3 FR1 FDD Conducted-Signal Tests  31 
3.2.3.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class NR testing Generic (NRG)  32 
Note that all downlink tests in this section use a 3GPP test wave form with 30 KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz 33 
Bandwidth as described in section 3GPP 38.141 -1 NR-FR1-TM1.1 and section 3.2.1.1.5 of this document.  There are 34 
several variations on this test signal depending on the capabilities of the radio.  If the radio does not support the 35 
numerology used in the example tests as reported in the M-plane it will be up to the test developer to modify their tests 36 
to adapt to the radio.  This can usually be accomplished by using stock test patters described above .  The test is 37 
expected to follow the same spirit as the tests in this document but things like symbol numbers, number of PRB s, etc. 38 
may have to be changed. 39 
All uplink tests in this section use a 3GPP test waveform described in 38.141 -1 section A1, in particular G-FR1-A5-1 40 
(30 kHz subcarrier spacing, QPSK, 100 MHz BW). As with downlink tests if the radio does not support this signal it is 41 
up to the test developer to modify the parameters of the test without changing the spirit of the test.  42

3.2.3.1.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Base 3GPP DL 1 
A. Test Description and Applicability 2 
This test is MANDATORY. 3 
 4 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can meet the most basic downlink requirements for O -RAN fronthaul.  5 
Subsequent tests will build on this to exercise additional capabilities of the Fronthaul.  6 
 7 
Using a standard 3GPP NR-FR1-TM1.1 test frame for FDD the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface of the TER 8 
described in section 2.1) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to transmit on the 9 
downlink the standard NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal.  This signal is shown below in Figure 3.2.3.1-1. 10 
 11 
 12 
Figure 3.2.3.1-1  NR-FR1-TM1.1 FDD Test Signal 13 
This test frame consists of a PDCCH in the first two symbols of every slot consisting of 3 PRBs.  All the 14 
remaining PRBs in the frame consist of Physical Downlink Shared Channel data. This configuration corresponds 15 
to stock data section A (Section 3.2.1.1.5 above) in all symbols that do not contain PDCCH channels. If the radio 16 
does not support the numerology described in section 3.2.3.1 the stock test frames can be adapted for smaller 17 
numbers of PRBs and should still be used. 18 
 19 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame using the defau lt parameters in 20 
section 3.2.1.1.5 of this document (or a similar 3GPP waveform) except only one spatial stream on one antenna 21 
will be used.  This test is applicable for Category A and Category B radios (No precoding is required).  As per 22 
TM-FR1-TM1.1 all user data in this test will be zeros. 23 
 24 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 25 
The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.1 of this document.  The test numerology will be 26 
30 KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth as described by TM-FR1-TM1.1.  It will be for 5G New 27 
Radio only. The radio must have conducted antenna ports (FR1) or TAB connectors.  28 
 29 
The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port (or TAB connector) to be connected to a signal analyzer.  It must 30 
also support the default parameters defined in section 3.2.1.1.1 above. 31 
 32 
C. Test Methodology 33 
a. Initial Conditions 34 
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 35 
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser to the 36 


 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
46 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
O-RU antenna port and configure the analyser with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and 1 
demodulate the transmitted signal.   2 
b. Procedure 3 
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 4 
emulator.  Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe 5 
the signal. Every symbol should be described by a single section (DL -SCH and DCI) using section type 1 6 
messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test.  Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane 7 
messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1.  8 
Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyser and allow it to 9 
demodulate and decode the test frame. 10 
 11 
 12 
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  13 
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance 14 
requirement for this radio category (i.e., EVM). 15 
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above.  If it 16 
contains all the same PRB assignments and all zero data, the test passes. 17

3.2.3.1.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Extended 3GPP DL – Resource allocation 19 
A. Test Description and Applicability 20 
This test is MANDATORY. 21 
 22 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can accurately interpret C-Plane resource allocation messages, 23 
transfer U-Plane data into the correct resource blocks and transmit this data accurately in the downlink.  This test is 24 
applicable for Category A and Category B radios (No precoding is required).  The test will be conducted therefore 25 
there will be no channel distortion or interference.  It is mandatory the radio pass this test to be considered O -RAN 26 
conformant. 27 
 28 
Using a standard 3GPP NR-FR1-TM1.1 test frame for FDD the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface of the TER 29 
described in section 2.1) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to transmit on the 30 
downlink the standard NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal.  This signal is shown below in Figure 3.2.3.1-2. 31 
 32 
 33

Figure 3.2.3.1-2  NR-FR1-TM1.1 FDD Test Signal 2

This test frame consists of a PDCCH in the first two symbols of every slot consisting of 3 PRBs.  All the remaining 4 
PRBs in the frame consist of Physical Downlink Shared Channel data. This test requires non -zero data (PN9 5 
Sequence)  to populate all allocated resource blocks.  This configuration corresponds to stock data section A in all 6

TM1.1.  It will be for 5G New Radio only. The radio must have conducted antenna ports (FR1) or TAB connectors.  11 
 12 
C. Testability requirements imposed on O-RU and O-DU 13 
The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port to be connected to a signal analyzer.  It must also support the 14 
default parameters defined in section 3.2.1.1.1 above.  The signal analyzer must have the ability to decode the 15 
downlink shared channel. 16 
 17 
D. Test Methodology 18 
 19 
a. Initial Conditions 20 
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 21 
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  Connect the signal analyser to the O-RU 22 
antenna port and configure the analyser with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and 23 
demodulate the transmitted signal.   24 
b. Procedure 25 
Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU emulator.  26 
Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal. 27 
Every symbol should be described by a single section (DL-SCH and DCI) using section type 1 messages. The 28 
data in the sections must be a PN9 sequence using an initial seed of all ones. No section type zero messages 29 
will be used for this test.  Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU 30 
respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1.  Repeat the entire frame the number of times 31 
required to synch the signal analyser and allow it to demodulate and decode the test frame.  32 
 33 
 34 
E. Test Requirement (expected result)  35 
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for 36 
this radio category (i.e., EVM). 37 
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above.  If it contains 38 
all the same PRB assignments and data, the test passes. 39

must be a PN9 sequence using an initial seed of all ones. The first bits of the PN9 will be in PRB1 and 19 
continue in consecutive resource elements to the end of PRB5. No section type zero messages will be 20 
used for this test. 21 
 22

PRBs 1 through 5.  The corresponding C-Plane message will contain a section IDs in a single C-Plane 24 
message describing symbol #6.  The startSymbolid in the application header will be symbol #6. The C-25 
Plane message will have one section with the reMask set to only the odd number res ource elements.  26 
The number of PRBs will be 4. The start PRB will be 1. 27

through 5 of symbol #6. 30

3.2.3.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming (BFM)  1 
This section describes the beamforming conformance testing for ORAN fronthaul interface. The tests do not aim to test 2 
the O-RU beamforming performance or capabilities but to test that the O-RU under test focuses the RF energy or 3 
sensitivity into a specific direction and with a specific granularity following the O-DU emulator (i.e., O-RAN interface 4 
of the TER described in section 2.1) C-Plane messages.  5 
Unless stated otherwise in a test case, the following statements apply to all the test cases defined in this section:  6 
• It is based on conducted testing with a setup such as described in Section 2.1 and it only applies to O-RU DUTs 7 
that have conducted antenna ports or TAB connectors. 8 
 9 
• It applies to Type A and Type B O-RU DUTs. 10 
 11 
• It applies to LTE and/or 5G New Radio O-RU DUTs.  In both cases, precoding is not required in any test case.   12 
 13 
• If O-RU DUT supports Analog Beamforming (i.e. time domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames are 14 
defined by segmenting the Stock Test A: 1 section per symbol.  The definition of this Stock Test A can be 15 
found in Figure 3.2.1.1-1 and the description accompanying this Figure.  Each slot shall include multiple 16 
sections (one per symbol within the slot) and only one beam at a time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore 17 
only one beam can be tested per slot. 18 
 19 
• If O-RU DUT supports Digital Beamforming (i.e. frequency domain beamforming), all the U-Plane test frames 20 
are defined by segmenting the Stock Test B: 2 sections per symbol definition as shown in Figure 3.2.1.1-1.  21 
Each slot shall include multiple sections (two per symbol within the slot) and only one beam per section at a 22 
time (i.e. one beamId at a time) and therefore up to two different beams can be tested per slot. 23 
 24 
• If O-RU DUT supports multiple polarizations, it is up to the TER to determine if the testing is carried out for 25 
each polarization separately or multiple polarizations at the same time. In any case, it is important to guarantee 26 
that the correct eAxC_ID for the correct polarization (or polarizations) is exercised.  27 
 28 
• For O-RU DUT that support LTE:  29 
o Downlink tests will use a standard 3GPP E-TM1.1 test frame for FDD (Section 6.1.1.1 TS136.141-1) with 30 
20MHz bandwidth (100 RB) as shown in Figure 3.2.3.2-1. 31 
 32 
Figure 3.2.3.2-1 E-TM1.1 FDD 20 MHz 100RB 33 
If 20MHz is not supported by the O-RU DUT, then it will use the highest bandwidth supported by the O-34 
RU DUT. 35 
o Uplink test will use a standard 3GPP UL RMC Configuration definition for FDD (TS36.521 -1) and 36 
power levels 30dB above Reference Sensitivity power level with 10MHz bandwidth (100 RB) as shown 37 
in Figure 3.2.3.2-2. 38 
 39 
Figure 3.2.3.2-2 UL RMC FDD 20 MHz 100 RB 40 
If 20MHz is not supported by the O-RU DUT, then it will use the highest bandwidth supported by the O-41 
RU DUT. 42

65 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
 1 
• For O-RU DUT that support 5G NR:  2 
o Downlink tests will use a standard 3GPP NR-FR1-TM1.1 test frame for FDD in [19] (Section 4.9.2 3 
TS138.141-1) of the Conducted Transmitter Characteristic Test section (Section 6 TS138.141 -1) as 4 
described in section 3.2.1.1. The test numerology will be preferably 30KHz subcarrier spacing and 100 5 
MHz Bandwidth. If not supported, then it will use any other supported subcarrier spacing and the 6 
highest bandwidth of the O-RU DUT. 7 
  8 
o Uplink tests will use a standard 3GPP Reference Sensitivity level definition (Section 7.2 and Annex A 9 
TS138.141-1) of the Conducted Receiver Characteristic Test section (Section 7 TS 138.141) and 10 
power levels 30dB above Reference Sensitivity power level as describe d in section 3.2.1.1.  The test 11 
numerology will be preferably 30kHz subcarrier spacing and 100 MHz Bandwidth, if supported. 12 
Otherwise, it will use any available subcarrier space and the highest bandwidth supported by the O-RU 13 
DUT. 14 
  15 
• The O-RU DUT must: 16 
o support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.1 of this document. 17 
o have installed current release of shipping software.  18 
o have at least two conducted antenna ports (or TAB connectors) to be connected to a signal analyzer. 19 
Likewise, it must have at least two conducted antenna ports or TAB connectors to be connected to a signal 20 
generator. 21 
o be fully calibrated up to the antenna ports or (TAB connectors) (if needed). It is expected to be calibrated 22 
by O-RU vendor prior to testing.  23 
 24 
 25 
• The TER must: 26 
o be capable of carrying out any signal processing required to generate and demodulate 3GPP compliant 27 
waveforms. 28 
o be able to calculate or extract beamweights (or magnitude and phase relations) between antenna ports or 29 
TAB connectors. Alternatively, and if the O-RU DUT manufacturer provides the list of beam directions 30 
supported by the O-RU DUT, TER might calculate or extract the beam direction instead of the 31 
beamweights. 32 
o be able to generate and deliver signals with the required beamweights (or magnitude and pha se relations) at 33 
the antenna ports or TAB connectors.  34 
o be fully calibrated up to the interfaces where is connected to the O-RU DUT antenna ports (or TAB 35 
connectors). For that, a known test signal might be either injected by the TER into the O -RU DUT, or 36 
internally generated by the O-RU DUT, and the O-RU DUT must not apply any digital or analog 37 
beamweights to the known test signal.  One possible method to perform calibration uses injected C-Plane 38 
and U-Plane signals from TER into the O-RU and using C-Plane messages with beamID=0.   39 
 40 
 41 
• The O-DU emulator of the TER must: 42 
o be capable of generating and sending U-Plane messages containing 3GPP test frames following the 43 
corresponding Stock sectioning defined above, as well as be capable of capturing U-Plane messages and 44 
extracting 3GPP test frames (i.e. IQ data) from the captured U-Plane messages. 45 
o be capable of generating the C-Plane messages for, receiving, extracting and demodulating the 3GPP test 46 
frames following the corresponding Stock sectioning defined above. 47 
 48 
• The TER might have less testing ports than the O-RU DUT conducted antenna ports (or TAB connectors) if 49 
testing is carried out sequentially; or as many antenna ports as the number of conducted antenna ports (or TAB 50 
connectors) under test if testing is carried out simultaneously. 51 
 52 
• It is up to the TER on how to extract the beamweights (or magnitude and phase relation) between the 53 
antenna ports or TAB connectors, or the beam direction / properties, in order to match it with the 54 
manufacturer’s declaration. 55 
 56 
• The user payload will be generated as PN9 with a seed of all ones. 57 
 58 
• It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections: 59 
• Section 5.4.2 for layout of C-Plane message, in particular Section Type 1 60

• Section 6.3.3 for coding of applicable Information Elements 2
