3.2.3.2.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – No Beamforming 6 
A. Test Description and Applicability 7 
This test is MANDATORY. 8 
 9 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 10 
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 11 
 12 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 13 
• Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of magnitude and phase relation (or beamweights) between 14 
antenna ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics when O-RU DUT 15 
is operating with no beamforming.  16 
 17 
C. Test Methodology 18 
 19 
a. Initial Conditions 20 
• Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 21 
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  22 
• Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence betw een the antenna 23 
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.  24 
• Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under 25 
test and configure the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 26 
transmitted signal.  27 
• Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  28 
 29 
b. Procedure 30 
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 31 
emulator.   32 
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 33 
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (DL-SCH 34 
and DCI) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test.  35 
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing 36 
windows described in section3.2.1.1.1.   37 
d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 38 
demodulate and decode the test frame. 39 
e. Extract either the beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation, or beam direction from the measured 40 
signal. 41 
 42 
 43 
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  44 
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for this 45 
radio category (i.e., EVM). 46 
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above and should 47 
contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN9 data. 48 
3. The signal relation (i.e. beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation) between a ntenna ports or TAB 49 
connectors, or the extracted beam direction, should match the expected relation, or beam direction, for the 50 
expected no beamforming within a tolerance defined by the manufacturer.  51 
 52 
3.2.3.2.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP UL – No Beamforming 53 
A. Test Description and Applicability 54 
This test is MANDATORY. 55 
 56 
 57 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
67 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can receive a basic 3GPP test frame with no beamforming 1 
(beamId=0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 2 
 3 
 4 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 5 
• Manufacturers’ declaration that defines list of magnitude and phase relation (or beamweights) between antenna 6 
ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics when O -RU DUT is 7 
operating with no beamforming.  8 
 9 
C. Test Methodology 10 
 11 
a. Initial Conditions 12 
• Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 13 
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. 14 
• Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 15 
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.  16 
• Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under test 17 
and configure the source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test 18 
signal.  19 
• Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   20 
 21 
b. Procedure 22 
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  23 
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial set of beamweights, or equivalently 24 
magnitude and phase relation, between all the TER ports connected to the antenna ports (or TAB 25 
connectors) to emulate the phase and magnitude difference “seen” by the antenna elements under test . For 26 
example, initial beamweights could be set to be “all equal” (i.e. no beamforming).  27 
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the 28 
signal and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by either one or two  sections (UL-29 
SCH) using section type 1 messages. No section type zero messages will be used for this test.  30 
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1. while 31 
also triggering the signal source.   32 
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 33 
plane messages to the O-DU and for the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload. 34 
f. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different set of beamweights or phase relation between 35 
all the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) when injecting the test signal into the O-RU. For example, 36 
repeating the process for a number of different beamweights will simulate the reception of the test signal 37 
from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O-RU is really focusing the sensitivity to 38 
the correct beam direction. 39 
 40 
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  41 
1. The test frame received by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signal described above and should contain 42 
all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN9 data. 43 
2. The beamweights or magnitude and phase relation at the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) of the test signal 44 
that achieves the highest performance (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) should match with the manufacturer’s 45 
declaration of the phase relation expected for no beamforming. 46 
 47 
3.2.3.2.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam 48 
Beamforming 49 
A. Test Description and Applicability 50 
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 51 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with predefined -beams 52 
beamforming (beamId≠0x000) and with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 53 
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each indexed beam required in this measurement, see below. The 54 
measured transmitted direction is compared to manufacturer-designated direction. Transmitted direction could be 55 
defined by the phase relation between the antenna ports or TAB connectors under test, or directly by extracting the 56 
beam direction. 57

Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
68 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
Depending on the O-RU beamforming capabilities regarding the ability to generate “coarse”, “fine” and/or “beam 1 
groups”, as defined in [2] Section 10.4.1.1. 2 
 3 
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in [2] Section 10.4.1.1: 4 
 5 
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Predefined-beam Beamforming conformance test 6 
might include multiple test that the O-RU must comply: 7 
a. “Coarse” beamIds test:  8 
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as coarse granularity (coars e beamIds) to the O-DU 9 
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 10 
1. A coarse beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 11 
2. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ).  12 
3. A coarse beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ).  13 
4. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ).  14 
5. A coarse beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 15 
 16 
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured.  17 
 18 
b.  “Fine” beamIds test:  19 
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that are defined as fine granularity (fine beamIds) to the O-DU 20 
emulator, the test should include the following beams: 21 
1. A fine beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles. 22 
2. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ).  23 
3. A fine beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle (θ).  24 
4. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle (θ).  25 
5. A fine beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevatio n angle (θ). 26 
 27 
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam angles will be measured.  28 
 29 
c.  “beam-group” beamIds test:  30 
If O-RU supports and reports beamIds that belong to same and different beam-groups to the O-DU emulator, 31 
the test should include the following beams: 32 
1. All beams that belong to a beam-group with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) or elevation (θ) angles. 33 
2. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 34 
3. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ). 35 
4. All beams that belong to a beam-group with maximum supported elevation angle (θ). 36 
5. All beams that belong to a beam-group with minimum supported elevation angle (θ). 37 
 38 
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth or elevation angle, fewer than 5 beam-groups will be measured. 39 
 40 
 41 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 42 
• Manufacturers’ defined list of beam indices and their associated magnitude and phase relation between antenna 43 
ports or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics. 44

transmitted signal.  55

 28 
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each weighted beam required in this measureme nt, see below. The 29

The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in [2] Section 10.4.1.1: 33

test should evaluate the following beams for the O-RU to comply: 37

(θ). 40

(θ). 42

(θ). 44

(θ). 46

 49

conformance test should also evaluate the following compression methods for each of the supported beams 51 
described above (a. to e.) for the O-RU to comply: 52 
a. No compression method applied to the beamforming weights.  53 
b. Block floating point compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit mantissa. 54 
c. Block scaling compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14 -bit scaler. 55 
d. μ-law compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14-bit fixed width. 56 
e. Beamspace compression method applied to the beamforming weights with 14 -bit scaler.  57

If the O-RU DUT supports Attribute based Dynamic Beamforming, this test is mandatory for  the O-RU DUT to be 1 
O-RAN conformant.   2 
The transmitted beam direction and attributes are measured for each attributed beam required in this measurement, 3 
see below. The measured transmitted direction and attributes, i.e. pointing azimuth and elevation angl es, 4 
beamwidths and sidelobe suppression, is compared to manufacturer-designated direction and attributes. 5 
Transmitted direction and beam attributes are defined by the magnitude and phase relation between the antenna 6 
ports or TAB connectors under test, or by directly extracting the beam properties. 7 
The elevation θ and azimuth Φ angles are defined as in Section 10.4.1.1  of [2]. 8 
 9 
 10 
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Attribute-based Dynamic Beamforming 11 
conformance test should evaluate the following beams for the O-RU to comply: 12 
a. An attribute-based beam with 0 degrees azimuth (Φ) and elevation (θ) angles with any beamwidth and sidelobe 13 
suppression supported by the O-RU under this beam direction. 14 
b. An attribute-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 15 
(θ) with the widest beamwidth and lowest sidelobe suppression supported for this specific beam direction.  16 
c. An attribute-based beam with maximum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 17 
(θ) with the narrowest beamwidth and highest sidelobe suppression supported for this specific beam direction.  18 
d. An attribute-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and maximum supported elevation angle 19 
(θ) with the widest beamwidth and lowest sidelobe suppression supported for this specific beam direction.  20 
e. An attribute-based beam with minimum supported azimuth angle (Φ) and minimum supported elevation angle 21 
(θ) with the narrowest beamwidth and highest sidelobe suppression supported for this specific beam direction.  22 
 23 
If the O-RU only supports one azimuth (Φ) or elevation angle (θ), fewer than 5 beam angles and attribute 24 
configurations will be measured. 25 
 26 
 27 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 28 
• Manufacturers’ defined list of supported beam directions (azimuth ϕ and elevation θ angles) attributes that are 29 
supported by the O-RU and their associated gain and phase relation, or complex weight, between antenna ports 30 
or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics.  31 
 32 
C. Test Methodology 33 
 34 
a. Initial Conditions 35 
• Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 36 
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.  37 
• Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 38 
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.   39 
• Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under 40 
test and configure the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 41 
transmitted signal.  42 
• Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   43 
 44 
b. Procedure 45 
a. Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the NR-FR1-TM1.1 signal described above in the O-DU 46 
emulator.   47 
b. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 48 
and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by one or two sections (DL-SCH and DCI) 49 
using section type 1 messages, the sections in the first symbol of the slot will contain section extension 50 
extType=0x02 to convey the beam weights, it is not required that the next sections contain extension type 2 51 
since the same beam IDs will not change along the slot.  If O-RU does not support a field, then its value 52 
should be 0x0. No section type zero messages will be used for this test. 53 
c. Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows 54 
described in section 3.2.1.1.1.   55 
d. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the signal analyzer and allow it to 56 
demodulate and decode the test frame. 57 
e. Extract either the beamweights, or magnitude and phase relation, or beam properties from the measured 58 
signal. 59

3.2.3.2.8 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP UL – Attribute-based Dynamic 11 
Beamforming 12 
A. Test Description and Applicability 13 
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 14 
 15 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can receive a basic 3GPP test frame with attribute -based beamforming 16 
with one spatial stream (single eAxC). 17 
 18 
Same description and criteria for selecting the beams to be tested applies as in section 3.2.3.2.7 but considering 19 
uplink direction.  20 
 21 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 22 
• Manufacturers’ defined list of supported beam directions (azimuth ϕ and elevation θ angles) attributes that are 23 
supported by the O-RU and their associated gain and phase relation, or complex weight, between antenna ports 24 
or TAB connectors and/or beam directions with antenna array characteristics 25 
 26 
C. Test Methodology 27 
 28 
a. Initial Conditions 29 
• Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 30 
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. 31 
• Ensure that the RF connections and cables are calibrated so there is phase coherence between the antenna 32 
ports (or TAB connectors) within acceptable tolerance.    33 
• Connect the signal source to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors that belong to the beam under test 34 
and configure the source with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and generate the test 35 
signal.  36 
• Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.   37 
 38 
b. Procedure 39 
a. Build an appropriate test signal described above in the signal source of the TER.  40 
b. Inject the test signal into the O-RU with the application of an initial set of beamweights, or equivalently 41 
magnitude and phase relation, between all the TER ports connected to the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) 42 
to emulate the phase and magnitude difference “seen” by the antenna elements under test . For example, 43 
initial beamweights could be set to be “all equal” (i.e. no beamforming).    44 
c. Use the O-DU emulator control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal 45 
and the beam under test. Every symbol should be described by one or two sections (UL-SCH) using section 46 
type 1 messages, the sections in the first symbol of the slot will contain section extension extType=0x02 to 47 
convey the beam weights, it is not required that the next sections contain extension type 2 since the same 48 
beam IDs will not change along the slot. If O-RU does not support a field, then its value should be 0x0. No 49 
section type zero messages will be used for this test. 50 
d. Play the C plane messages to the O-RU respecting timing windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1. while also 51 
triggering the signal source.   52 
e. Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the DUT, allow it to create and send the U 53 
plane messages to the O-DU and for the O-DU to demodulate, decode and extract the payload. 54 
f. Repeat the previous steps but now in step b apply a different set of beamweights or magnitude and phase 55 
relation between all the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) when injecting the test signal into the O -RU. For 56 
example, repeating the process for a number of different set of beamweights will simulate the reception of 57

the test signal from different beam directions. This allows to determine if the O -RU is really focusing the 1

D. Test Requirement (expected result)  4 
1. The test frame received by the TER/O-DU should be the same as the signal described above and should 5 
contain all the same PRB assignments and all the original PN9 data. 6 
2. The beamweights or magnitude and phase relation at the antenna ports (or TAB connectors) of the test signal 7 
that achieves the highest performance (i.e. best EVM, power, SNR, etc.) should match with the 8 
manufacturer’s declaration of the beam under test. 9

3.2.3.2.9 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Channel-Information-based 11 
Beamforming 12 
A. Test Description and Applicability 13 
This Test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY. 14 
 15 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame with channel -information-based 16 
beamforming with multiple spatial streams from multiple users (i.e. MU -MIMO). 17 
 18 
For Category A radios, the test is for each polarization separately and consequently either different or same channel 19 
models can be defined for each of the polarization. For Category B, same channel might be used for both 20 
polarizations and the test might measure each polarization separately. 21 
The transmitted beam direction is measured for each scenario required in this measurement .  The measured 22 
transmitted direction is extracted from the decoded received signal in the TER. Transmitted direction is defined by 23 
properly receiving a data transmission between the O-RU and the target User Equipment while destroying or 24 
heavily attenuating the data transmission between the O-RU and the other User Equipment. 25 
The UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Beamforming 3GPP DL – Channel-Information-based Beamforming 26 
conformance test should evaluate the following scenarios for the O-RU to comply and will rely on TER Channel 27 
Emulation capabilities as shown in Figure 3.2.3.2-3.  28

3.2.3.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Compression (CMP) 1 
Validate the correct implementation and interpretation of mandatory and optional IQ data compression formats 2 
described in [2]. Also, evaluate the consistency in U-Plane signaling. 3 
It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections in [2]: 4 
• Section 5.4.2 for layout of C-Plane message, in particular Section Type 1 5 
• Section 5.4.4.10 for applicability of "udCompHdr" and "reserved" fields 6 
• Section 6.3.3.15/16/17 for applicability of udCompParam 7 
• Section 6.3.2 for U-Plane message layout 8 
• Section 6.3.3 for coding of applicable Information Elements 9 
• Table 8-2 for mandatory/optional capabilities. 10 
• Annex A  11 
 12 
The objective is primarily to test the protocol, prior to the compression algorithms performance.  13 
Signalling: IQ Compression related fields in UC-Plane messages include:  14 
• U-Plane IQ data field  15 
• C-Plane udCompHdr (per section 5.4.4.10 of [2]) 16 
• U-Plane udComphdr (per section 6.3.3.13 of [2]) 17 
• U-Plane udCompParam (per section 6.3.3.15 of [2]) 18 
 19 
Compression: Current specification includes 5 compression modes, including uncompressed mode (fixed point).  Tests 20 
should cover each one of these modes   21 
• fixed-point 22 
• block floating-point 23 
• block scaling 24 
• mu-law 25 
• modulation compression (modulation compression not included in this document)  26 
 27 
IQ Bit Width: IQ information can be represented using different bit width (1-16 bits). To optimize test time, tests 28 
should be performed on a subset of bit widths  29 
• 9 bits 30 
• 14 bits  31 
3.2.3.3.1 Overview of Compression Test Methodology 32 
A common test methodology and structure will be used across all compression test cases. Each one of the test cases will 33 
be defined with specific input parameters and expected output values.  34 
To minimize influence of the Radio’s RF performance to the test results, the test methodology will be based on a 35 
relative comparison between modulated signal measurements performed on a test frame with uncompressed IQ (fixed 36 
16 bits) and measurements on the same test frame using compressed IQ. The test will verify that the difference between 37 
measurements fits within an acceptable range for the test to pass. 38 
For downlink test, the modulated signal measurement is performed by a signal analyser on the antenna port of the O -39 
RU.  40 
For uplink measurement, the modulated signal measurement is performed with the IQ extracted from the Uplink U-41 
Plane data sent by the O-RU on the O-RAN interface.  42 
The following paragraphs in this overview section outline the details of these common test methodologies.  43 
3.2.3.3.1.1 Test Frame 44 
The test frames used for compression conformance test will be referred in this document as “NR-FR1-CMP-TST-45 
FRAME-DL” Downlink Standard Compression Test frame and “NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-UL” Uplink Standard 46 
Compression Test frame. They are 5G NR frames based on the description in section 3.2.1.1.5 with specific attributes 47 
described below. 48

3.2.3.3.1.2 Test Frame Power  3 
To ensure that the compressed IQ exponent value is properly tested, each symbol of the test frame will include 3 4 
sections with different power levels.  The Power levels are relative powers to the first group of PRBs transmitted.  Any 5 
valid 3GPP power level may be used for the first set of PRBs as long as the power levels of the remaining PRBs are 6 
also valid.  Figure 3.2.3.3-1 below shows PRB power relative to the first set of PRBs. 7 
•    0 dB for the bottom third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH0) 8 
• -10 dB for the middle third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH1) 9 
• -20 dB for the upper third of total PRBs in the symbol (referred as PDSCH2)  10 
 11 
The spectrum representation of the frame shown in Figure 3.2.3.3-1 below highlights the various power levels for each 12 
group of PRBS within a symbol.  13 
 14

3.2.3.3.1.3 Test Frame User data  1 
To validate that user data has not been impacted by compression, the test payload for the 3 sections is based on a PN9 2 
sequence that will be measured and compared by the test apparatus.   3 
3.2.3.3.1.4 Test Frame Modulation Scheme 4 
To maximise coverage on the compressed IQ mantissa value, the test frame will use the highest possible modulation 5 
(256 QAM modulation for downlink).  An example measurement is show in Figure 3.2.3.3-2. 6 
 7

3.2.3.3.1.5 Summary of Required Measurements for Compression Tests 9 
3 measurements types will be required for downlink tests and 4 measurements will be required for uplink tests.  10 
• Power level:  Using the test frames (NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-DL and NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-UL) 11 
sent twice with both compressed and uncompressed IQ data, power level measurements are performed  to 12 
validate compression algorithms influence on Exponent (udCompParam).  13 
The Power level measurements are called: 14 
 15 
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 in dBm 16 
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 in dBm 17 
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH1 in dBm 18 
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH1 in dBm 19 
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH2 in dBm 20 
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH2 in dBm 21 
 22 
For the test to pass, the difference between measurements should be within an acceptable range, called 23 
o ACC_PWR_PDSCH0 = ± 1dB 24 
o ACC_PWR_PDSCH1 = ± 1dB 25 
o ACC_PWR_PDSCH2 = ± 1dB 26 
o  27 
• EVM:  Using a common test frame sent twice with both compressed and uncompressed IQ data, EVM 28 
measurements comparisons between uncompressed IQ and compressed IQ will help validate acceptable 29 
compression influence on signal quality.  30 
 31 
These 6 EVM measurements required: 32 
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH0 in % 33 
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH0  in % 34 
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH1  in % 35 
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH1  in % 36 
o CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH2  in % 37 
o CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH2  in % 38 
 39 
For the test to pass, the difference between the compressed and uncompressed measurements for the same 40 
PDSCH signal must be within the following range: 41 
o ACC_EVM_PDSCH0 ≤ 4 percentage points 42 
o ACC_EVM_PDSCH1 ≤ 4 percentage points 43 
o ACC_EVM_PDSCH2 ≤ 4 percentage points 44 
 45 
An example measurement showing both power and EVM is shown below in Figure 3.2.3.3-3. 46

• Payload Data Integrity:  comparing user data between the O-RAN test frame and the RF measurement to 3 
validate that compression does not influence user data.  The User data measurements are called: 4 
 5 
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH0  6 
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH1  7 
o CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH2  8 
o CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH0  9 
o CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH1  10 
o CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH2  11 
 12 
For the data integrity test to pass, the comparison between stimulus payload and the measured payload should 13 
be free of any errors (i.e. BER=0).  14 
 15 
• Presence/Absence of U-Plane Header measurements (uplink only): to validate that in the U-Plane PRB 16 
header, the udCompHeader, “reserved” and udCompParam fields are correctly absent for Static compression 17 
mode or present for other compression modes.  18

3.2.3.3.1.7 Results Analysis 4 
In general, for each specific Compression Test in this conformance test document, the test will pass if the following 5 
conditions are met: 6 
• Power measurement differences between Uncompressed and Compressed are within acceptable range  7 
• EVM measurement difference between Uncompressed and Compressed are within acceptable range  8 
• Data integrity measurements show no data corruption 9 
• Uplink U-Plane Header measurements exclude fields for static compression 10 
 11 
These test criteria and expected results are summarized below in Table 3.2.3.3-6. 12

3.2.3.3.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Compression Static Format (SFM) Fixed-Point (FP)  3 
A. Test Description and Applicability 4 
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY and should be performed if the O-RU supports this compression 5 
format. 6 
 7 
The purpose of this test is to: 8 
• Validate correct encoding of IQ data under the following conditions.  9 
o RU Static compression configurations 10 
o Fixed point IQ data format 11 
o Selection of 2 supported bit width: 9 bits, 14 bits  12 
o Uplink / downlink 13 
• Validate that in the U-Plane PRB header, the udCompHeader, “reserved” and udCompParam fields are 14 
not present  15 
 16 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 17 
 The test uses the setup and methodology described in section 3.2.1.1. 18 
 19 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
87 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
 1 
C. Test Methodology 2 
a.  Initial Conditions 3 
• The O-RU is started 4 
• Fronthaul Ethernet interface configured for communication between TER and the DUT. 5 
• O-RU synchronized with TER using S-Plane 6 
• Communication established between TER and the DUT such that it is possible to exchange U-Plane and 7 
C-Plane messages  8 
• Signal Analyzer connected to DUT’s antenna port and setup according to DUT RF output configuration  9 
• Signal Source connected to DUT’s antenna port and setup according to DUT RF input configuration 10 
 11 
b.  Procedure 12 
For each supported bit width (9 bits, 14 bits), the following tests need to be performed:  13 
  14 
1. Downlink test 15 
• Via the M-Plane or another suitable mechanism, put the O-RU into a static configuration with the 16 
downlink configured as follows: no compression, (16 bits) 17 
• Arm Signal Analyzer to capture the next Frame  18 
• Send the “uncompressed” NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-ST-DL-UNC-16B test stimulus file to the 19 
DUT 20 
• With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 power measurements  21 
• CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 in dBm 22 
• CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH1 in dBm 23 
• CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH2 in dBm 24 
• With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 EVM measurements  25 
• CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH0 in % 26 
• CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH1 in % 27 
• CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH2 in % 28 
• With the Signal Analyzer, check Data integrity measurements  29 
• CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH0  30 
• CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH1  31 
• CMP-Uncompressed-BER-PDSCH2  32 
• Via the M-Plane or another suitable mechanism, put the O-RU into a static configuration with the 33 
downlink configured as follows: Fixed point, 9-bit (then 14 bits)  34 
• Send the “Compressed” NR-FR1-CMP-TST-FRAME-ST-DL-FPF-9B (then 14B) test stimulus 35 
file to the DUT 36 
• With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 power measurements  37 
• CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 in dBm 38 
• CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH1 in dBm 39 
• CMP-Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH2 in dBm 40 
• With the Signal Analyzer, perform the 3 EVM measurements  41 
• CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH0 in % 42 
• CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH1 in % 43 
• CMP-Compressed-Measured-EVM-PDSCH2 in % 44 
• With the Signal Analyzer, check Data integrity measurements  45 
• CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH0  46 
• CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH1  47 
• CMP-Compressed-BER-PDSCH2  48 
• Verify the following conditions  49 
• Power measurements within acceptable range  50 
• Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 and CMP-51 
Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH0 is within ACC_PWR_PDSCH0 range 52 
• Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH1 and CMP-53 
Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH1 is within ACC_PWR_PDSCH1 range 54 
• Difference between CMP-Uncompressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH2 and CMP-55 
Compressed-Measured-Power-PDSCH2 is within ACC_PWR_PDSCH2 range 56 
•  57 
 58 
• EVM  measurements within acceptable range  59

3.2.3.4 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Delay Management (DLM) 2 
This section describes conformance test cases for O-RU Delay Management. 3 
The test setup for these test cases is shown in 2.1.  4 
When performing the conformance test cases for scenario class Delay Management it does not matter which timing 5 
method is used. The different timing methods are described in section 2.3.2, 2.3.3, 2.3.4 and 2.3.5 in the CUS 6 
Specification [2] 7 
Delay Management downlink tests will test whether the O-RU can accurately transmit data when C and U plane 8 
message are received at the extreme ends of their respective reception windows. Uplink tests will test whether the O-RU 9 
can accurately transmit received data to the CUSM-E when the CUSM-E transmits uplink C-Plane messages within the 10 
correct uplink reception window.  It also tests whether the O-RU sends its U-Plane messages within the correct 11 
reception window. 12 
Figure 3.2.3.4-1 shows a simplified timing relation for the C- and U-Plane messages for downlink. 13 
The size of the control plane reception window on the O-RU will be: (T2a_max_up +Tcp_adv_dl) – (T2a_min_up 14 
+Tcp_adv_dl) = C-Plane reception window.   The start-point (before t=0) will be: T2a_max_up + Tcp_adv_dl = start of 15 
C-Plane transmission window. 16 
The size of the reception window for the user plane will be: T2a_max_up - T2a_min_up.The start-point (before t=0) 17 
will beT2a_max_up. 18 
As an example, if the values are set such as T2a_max_up = 264 µs, Tcp_adv_dl = 63 µs and T2a_min_up = 53 µs, then 19 
the C-Plane reception window would be 211 µs, the start of C-plane transmission window would be 327 us, the U-plane 20 
reception window would 211 µs and the start of U-plane transmission window would be 264 µs. 21 
 22

The Delay Management uplink test cases for the O-RU will test that if the C-Plane fronthaul messages is received with 1 
respective reception window then the corresponding U-Plane messages will be sent in the O-RU’s transmission 2 
window. 3 
Figure 3.2.3.4-2 shows a simplified timing relation for the C-Plane and U-Plane messages for uplink. 4 
Similar to the downlink case, the size of the control plane reception window is T2a_max_cp_ul - T2a_min_cp_ul . The 5 
start-point of (before t=0) of the C-plane reception window is T2a_max_cp_ul. 6 
The size of the transmission window for the user plane will be: Ta3_max_up  - Ta3_min_up. The start-point (after t=0) 7 
will be Ta3_min_up. 8 
If we follow the same example values as the ones set in the downlink case, the C-plane reception window would be 211 9 
µs, the start-point of the C-plane reception window would be 274 µs, the U-plane transmission window would be 70 µs 10 
and the start-point of the U-plane transmission window would be 20 µs.  11

3.2.3.4.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class DLM Test #1: Downlink – Positive testing 1 
A. Test Description and Applicability 2 
This test is MANDATORY. 3 
 4 
This test case will validate that the timing on the air interface is according to requirements specified in the 5 
CUS Specification when the C-Plane and the U-Plane messages are received within the O-RU’s reception 6 
windows. 7 
 8 
Four different test cases for downlink can be performed when the expected outcome is positive, i.e. the O-RU 9 
shall be able to transmit the received U-Plane-data on the air interface.  These are shown in Figure 3.2.3.4-5.  10 
Note that in these tests the C-Plane reception window may be applicable to the slot or symbol boundaries 11 
depending on the Radio’s capabilities.  That is, in some radios, the C-Plane reception window is at the 12 
beginning of each slot and all C-Plane messages will be sent at once within this window.  Other radios will 13 
require C-Plane messages to be sent in a reception window for each symbol, In all cases U-Plane messages will 14 
be sent during reception windows corresponding to each symbol regardless of whether the radio has large 15 
enough buffers to store U-Plane data for multiple symbols. 16

1st case “C-Plane Early – U-Plane Early”; the C-Plane message is received by the O-RU at the beginning of 21

2nd case “C-Plane Early – U-Plane Late”; the C-Plane message is received by the O-RU at the beginning of 25 
the reception window for the C-Plane messages. The corresponding U-Plane data is received earliest Tcp_adv_dl 26 
after the C-Plane message i.e. in the end of the U-Plane reception window. 27

3rd case “C-Plane Late – U-Plane Early”; the C-Plane message is received by the O-RU at the end of the 1 
reception window for the C-Plane messages.  The corresponding U-Plane data is received earliest Tcp_adv_dl 2 
after the C-Plane message i.e. in the end of the reception window. 3 
4th case “C-Plane Late – U-Plane Late”; this case is greyed out in the figure since it will in practice be the 4 
same case as number 3, the U-Plane message cannot be received later than it is in case 3. 5

 7 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 8 
The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port (or TAB connector) to be connected to a signal analyzer.  The 9 
reception windows will be calculated and used by the CUSM-E based on the delay parameters reported by the 10 
radio on the M-Plane. 11 
 12 
C. Test Methodology 13 
 14 
a. Initial Conditions 15 
Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 16 
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1. Connect the RF Signal 17 
Analyzer to the O-RU antenna port. Determine the correct reception windows the radio claims to 18 
support using delay management parameters repowered by the radio, 19 
b. Procedure 20 
Configure the CUSM-ECUSM-E to send C-Plane and U-Plane messages so these messages are received 21 
within the reception windows for respective plane according to the three cases (1..3) described in figure 22 
above. NOTE: Make sure that the C-Plane message is received at least Tcp_adv_dl earlier then the 23 
corresponding U-Plane message(s) by the O-RU. 24 
 25 
On the RF-signal-analyzer observe the received signal and compare the decoded data on the selected test 26 
symbol to the send PN9 sequence for that symbol. 27 
 28 
D. Pass/Fail Criteria (expected result) 29 
The test passes if the received data matches the transmitted data. 30 
 31 
3.2.3.4.2 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class DLM Test #2: Uplink – Positive testing 32 
A. Purpose and Description  33 
This test is MANDATORY. 34 
 35 
This test case will validate that the transmission of the U-Plane data in uplink direction are transmitted correctly by 36 
the O-RU within its transmission window.  The CUSM-E will send C-Plane messages at both ends of the C-Plane 37 
reception window specified by the radio using the M-Plane (Two tests).  The C-Plane messages will describe a test 38 
frame as shown above.  The frame will have one designated symbol in each slot (not containing DMRS 39 
information).  The C-Plane message will ask the radio to send that symbol’s data from each slot. 40 
 41 
After the correct C-Plane messages are sent the CUSM-E will trigger the signal generator to send a valid test signal 42 
to the radio’s RF port.  This signal will contain a new, known PN9 sequence in the same symbol (per slot) 43 
designated by the C-Plane messages. 44 
 45 
The positive test outcome for these uplink test cases is that the corresponding U-Plane data for a specific C-Plane 46 
message is transmitted within the O-RU’s transmission window IF the C-Plane message was received within the O-47 
RU’s reception window as shown in Figure 3.2.3.4-6 48 
.  The data will be transmitted to the radio by an external signal generator and the uplink signal will be as described 49 
above.  The test data sent by the signal generator will contain a known, new PN9 sequence in one symbol of each 50 
slot.  The CUSM-E will expect to receive the same data for the correct symbol in each slot. 51

3.2.3.4.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class DLM Test #3: Downlink – Negative testing 8 
A. Test Description and Applicability 9 
This test is MANDATORY. 10 
 11 
This test case will validate that the O-RU will correctly increment relevant M-Plane counters if C-Plane and/or U-12 
Plane messages are not received within the respective O-RU reception windows. 13 
 14 
Negative testing for downlink traffic will verify that the O-RU will correctly increment relevant M-Plane counters 15 
if C-Plane and/or U-Plane messages are not received within the respective O-RU reception windows.  There are 16 
four test cases defined for this Downlink test and are shown in Figure 3.2.3.4-8.  The titles on each diagram show 17 
the message arrival time relative to the O-RU receive window for the C-Plane and the U-Plane in that order.  For 18 
instance, test 1: Too Early-OK means the C-Plane message arrived early, outside the O-RU C-Plane receive 19 
window and the corresponding U-Plane message arrived correctly within the O-RU U-Plane receive window.  20 
 21 
1: Too Early - OK t=0
T2a_max_cp_dl
T2a_max_up_dl
Tcp_adv_dl
O-RU rec. win. C -plane

3.2.3.4.4 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class DLM Test #4: Uplink – Negative Testing 17

This test is MANDATORY. 19 
 20

Plane messages are not received within the respective O-DU reception windows. 22 
 23 
Negative testing for uplink traffic will verify that the O-RU will correctly increment relevant M-Plane counters if 24 
C-Plane and/or U-Plane messages are not received within the respective O-DU reception windows.  There are four 25 
test cases defined for this Downlink test and are shown in Figure 3.2.3.4-9.  The titles on each diagram show the 26 
message arrival time relative to the O-RU receive window for the C-Plane and the U-Plane in that order.  For 27 
instance, test 1: Too Early-OK means the C-Plane message arrived early, outside the O-RU C-Plane receive 28 
window and the corresponding U-Plane message arrived correctly within the O-RU U-Plane receive window. 29 
Negative testing for uplink traffic will verify that the O-RU will not transmit any U-Plane uplink data when C-30 
Plane messages are not received within the window on the O-RU. 31

3.2.3.6 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class LAA (LAA) 17 
The purpose of this section is to specify LAA test cases to test the compliance of the O-RU to the O-RAN 18 
specifications. Although in LAA operation, regular C-Plane and U-Plane messages (used for operation over licensed 19 
spectrum as well) are transmitted over the fronthaul interface between the O-DU and O-RU, there exist additional C-20 
Plane messages that are required specifically for LAA operation over unlicensed spectrum. These additional C-Plane 21 
messages are based on Section type 7 and are communicated in both UL and DL direction s between the O-DU and O-22 
RU.  23 
 24 
The LAA test cases only focus on LAA-related messages and operations. Other testing aspects that are applicable to 25 
LAA and non-LAA technologies (e.g., delay management, beamforming, compression, etc.) are not considered in th is 26 
section; Please refer to other sections in the conformance test specification document.  27 
 28 
LAA considered in this section is based on 3GPP Rel. 13, which only considers downlink transmission on the 29 
unlicensed spectrum (i.e., uplink transmission goes on the licensed component carrier). Hence, all the test cases in this 30 
section will consider downlink operation only. This includes DL U-Plane messages and DL/UL C-Plane messages. Note 31 
also that UL C-Plane messages only exist in LAA technology. 32 
 33 
The LAA test cases for the O-RU test if the O-RU is capable of conforming with the CUSM-E instructions in terms of: 34 
1) Correctly performing the listen-before-talk (LBT) procedure (i.e., managing the congestion window). 35 
2) Timely data transmission based on the spectrum sensing outcome. 36 
3) Timely deferring from occupying the spectrum based on the messages received from the O -DU. 37 
 38 
On the other hand, testing O-RU capabilities (e.g., spectrum sensing) is out of scope of this specifications since it’s not  39 
directly related to the O-RAN fronthaul interface.  40 
 41 
3.2.3.6.1 CU-DU-LAA-CWM Test #1: LBT PDSCH Configuration and Response  42 
A. Test Description and Applicability 43 
This test is CONDITIONAL MANDATORY.  The test must be executed if the O-RU supports LAA. 44 
This test validates that the O-RU is capable of the following functions 45 
• Correctly receiving and interpreting C-Plane messages (Section Type 7 and specifically laaMsgType 0) 46 
from the TER to correctly perform LBT.  47 
• Correctly receiving U-Plane data from the TER and correctly processes the data (i.e., drop it or transmit 48 
it) based on the LBT outcome.  49 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
104 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
• Correctly performing LBT and correctly generating C-Plane messages to inform the TER about the LBT 1 
outcomes using Section Type 7 and specifically laaMsgType 2. 2 
 3 
This test assumes that the O-RU is capable of processing Section Type 1 C-plane messages and its corresponding 4 
U-plane messages. 5 
It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections: 6 
• Section 5.4.2 for layout of C-Plane messages, in particular Section Type 1 and Section Type 7. 7 
• Section 5.4.5.14 for applicability of “laaMsgType” (LAA message type) 8 
• Section 5.4.5.15 for applicability of “laaMsgLen” (LAA message length) 9 
• Section 5.4.5.16 for applicability of “lbtHandle” (LBT Handle) 10 
• Section 5.4.5.17 for applicability of “lbtDeferFactor” (listen-before-talk defer factor) 11 
• Section 5.4.5.18 for applicability of “lbtBackoffCounter” (listen-before-talk backoff counter) 12 
• Section 5.4.5.19 for applicability of “lbtOffset” (listen-before-talk offset) 13 
• Section 5.4.5.20 for applicability of “MCOT” (maximum channel occupancy time)  14 
• Section 5.4.5.21 for applicability of “lbtMode” (LBT Mode) 15 
• Section 5.4.5.22 for applicability of “lbtPdschRes” (LBT PDSCH Result)  16 
• Section 5.4.5.23 for applicability of “sfStatus” (subframe status) 17 
• Section 5.4.5.25 for applicability of “initialPartialSF” (Initial partial SF) 18 
• Section 5.4.5.27 for applicability of “sfnSf” (SFN/SF End) 19 
• Table 8-2 for mandatory capabilities 20 
 21 
The purpose of this test is to: 22 
• Validate that the O-RU can correctly interpret C-Plane messages by correctly performing LBT.  23 
• Validate that the O-RU can correctly construct the UL C-Plane message as specified in Section Type 7, 24 
laaMsgType 2 with the following specialized fields. Specifically,  25 
o Verify the laaMsgLen based on the message content. 26 
o Verify that the lbtHandle parameter in the DL C-Plane message with laaMsgType 0 matches the 27 
corresponding lbtHandle parameter in the UL C-Plane message with laaMsgType 2.  28 
o Verify the lbtPdschRes parameter value. Set: {0, 1, 2, 3}. 29 
o Verify the inParSF parameter value. Set: {0, 1} 30 
o Verify the sfStatus parameter value. Set: {0, 1}.  31 
o Verify the sfnSf value.  32 
• Validate that the O-RU can correctly interpret U-Plane data received from the TER. 33 
• Validate that the O-RU can correctly interpret C-Plane messages received from the TER.  34 
 35 
 36 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 37 
• The O-RU must support LAA 38 
• The O-RU has passed M-Plane conformance and S-Plane conformance testing. 39 
• The O-RU has antenna ports or TAB connectors for TER connections 40

C. Test Methodology 42 
The test shall be executed by the TER issuing DL C-Plane messages to the O-RU DUT to cause the O-RU to 43 
execute LBT. Furthermore, the TER shall issue other U-Plane and C-Plane messages required for data 44 
transmission. The TER needs to emulate external interference to allow the O-RU to do LBT and send the LBT 45 
outcome to the TER based on the description in Section 5.3.4 in [2] 46 
 47 
a. Initial Conditions 48 
• TER (Test Equipment, O-RU) is initialized and configured. 49 
• The O-RU is initialized, synchronized, and configured as normal, except that it shall receive and interpret 50 
Test Commands. 51 
• The fronthaul Ethernet interface is up. 52 
•  The O-RU is running its usual software, except that it is configured to accept and execute Test Commands 53 
to enable O-RU Conformance Testing. 54 
• The TER needs to emulate the external interference (e.g., Wi-Fi, other LAA cells) for the O-RU to execute 55 
LBT.  56

b. Procedure 58

3.2.3.7 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class LTE (LTE) 5 
This section describes applicable LTE conformance test cases for O-RAN fronthaul interface. Since there are plenty of 6 
the commonalities between the NR and LTE test cases, this section makes suitable references to the NR specific test 7 
cases sections for the LTE scenarios whenever possible, as below.   8 
• LTE UC-Plane O-DU Scenario Class Beamforming (BFM) described in clause 3.2.3.2 9 
• LTE UC-Plane O-DU Scenario Class Compression (CMP) described in clause 3.2.3.3 10 
• LTE UC-Plane O-DU Scenario Class Delay Management (DLM) described in clause 3.2.3.4 11 
• LTE UC-Plane O-DU Scenario Class LAA (LAA) described in clause 3.2.3.6 12 
• LTE UC-Plane O-DU Scenario Class Section Type 3 described in clause 3.2.3.8 13 
 14 
Subsequently, LTE-only specific generic test cases are explicitly covered in the subsections below.  One of the key 15 
differences applicable for LTE specific test cases as compared to NR is due to the explicit precoding behavior supported 16 
by some of the transmission modes for LTE.  17 
In particular, for a Category B O-RU to implement precoding for LTE TM2-TM4, specific C-Plane instructions need to 18 
be provided to the O-RU from the O-DU.  This specific aspect of the O-RAN fronthaul interface is enabled by the 19 
section extension = 0x3 described in the CUS Plane specification [2]. 20 
For all the test cases described in this section: 21 
▪ Downlink tests will use a standard 3GPP E-TM1.1 test frame for FDD (Section 6.1.1.1 TS136.141-1) as shown in 22 
Figure 3.2.3.7-1. 23 
 24 
Figure 3.2.3.7-1 3GPP E-TM1.1 Test Frame for FDD 25

▪ Uplink tests will use a standard 3GPP UL RMC Configuration definition for FDD (TS36.521 -1) and power levels 27 
30dB above Reference Sensitivity power level as shown in Figure 3.2.3.7-2 UL RMC Configuration for FDD: 28

There are several variations on this test signal depending on the capabilities of the radio.  If for example the radio does 5 
not support the bandwidth used in the example tests as reported in the M -plane it will be up to the test developer to 6

3.2.3.7.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Base 3GPP DL 12 
A. Test Description and Applicability 13 
This test is MANDATORY. 14 
  15 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can transmit a basic 3GPP test frame using the default parameters in 16 
section 3.2.1.1.1 of this document except for only one spatial stream on one antenna will be used.   17 
 18 
This test is applicable for Type A and Type B radios (No precoding is required).   19 
As per E-TM1.1 all user data in this test will be zeros.  The test will be conducted.   20 
 21 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 22 
• The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1.1.1 of this document.  The test bandwidth is 20 23 
MHz Bandwidth as described by E-TM1.1. 24 
• The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port to be connected to a signal analyzer.   25 
• The signal analyzer must have the ability to decode the downlink shared channel.  26 
 27 
C. Procedure 28 
a. Initial Conditions 29 
• Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation using 30 
M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.   31 
• Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors under test and configure the 32 
analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the transmitted signal.  33 
• Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  34 
 35 
b. Procedure 36 
• Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the E-TM1.1 signal described above in the CUSM-E.  37 
• Use the CUSM-E control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal. 38 
Every symbol should be described by a single section (DL-SCH and DCI) using section type 1 messages.  39 
• The data in the sections must be a PN9 sequence using an initial seed of all ones.  40 
• No section type zero messages will be used for this test.  41 
• Encapsulate the IQ data in U-Plane messages. Play those messages to the O-RU respecting timing 42 
windows described in section 3.2.1.1.1.  Repeat the entire frame the number of times required to synch the 43 
signal analyser and allow it to demodulate and decode the test frame. 44 
 45

                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  1 
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performan ce requirement for 2 
this radio category (i.e., EVM). 3 
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should be the same as the signal described above.  If it contains 4 
all the same PRB assignments and all zero data, the test passes. 5

3.2.3.7.3 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Extended 3GPP UL – Resource Allocation 50 
A. Test Description and Applicability 51 
This test is MANDATORY. 52 
 53 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance.

109 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
The purpose of this test is to validate correct uplink operation of the O-RU using 3GPP Reference Sensitivity 1 
level definition (Section 7.2 TS 136.141) of the Conducted Receiver Characteristic Test section (Section 7 TS 2 
36.104) and power Levels at least 30 dB above Reference Sensitivity power Level described in E-TM1.1.  This 3 
is to improve the likelihood that all data will be received by the radio correctly since we are not interested in 4 
testing receiver sensitivity but only the O-RAN protocol compliance.  5 
 6 
Under those conditions, 3GPP compliant O-RU should deliver uplink U-Plane information that matches with 7 
the uplink signal.  8 
 9 
The TER (Test Equipment, O-RU) generates an uplink signal on the antenna connector or TAB connector, 10 
together with the corresponding C-Plane messages on the Fronthaul interface. The TER will capture the U-11 
Plane messages generated by the DUT and validate if the payload matches with the uplink signal.   12 
 13 
This test is applicable for both Type A and Type B radios. 14 
 15 
It applies to the following CUS fronthaul specification sections 16 
• Section 5.4.2 for layout of C-Plane message, in particular Section Type 1 17 
• Section 6.3.2 for U-Plane message layout 18 
• Section 6.3.3 for coding of applicable Information Elements 19 
 20 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 21 
 22 
• The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1 of this document.  The test bandwidth is 20 23 
MHz Bandwidth as described by E-TM1.1. 24 
• The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port to be connected to a signal analyzer.   25 
• The signal analyzer must have the ability to decode the downlink shared channel.  26 
• The Radio must support the reMask parameter as notified by the M-Plane.  27 
 28 
C. Test Methodology 29 
 30 
a. Initial Conditions 31 
• Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for 32 
operation using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.   33 
• Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors under test and configure 34 
the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the 35 
transmitted signal.  36 
• Configure the source to transmit the required 3GPP test signal upon receiving a trigger signal from 37 
the CUSM-ECUSM-E.  The signal source power level should be adjusted to setting used in the 38 
3GPP receiver sensitivity test. 39 
• Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  40 
 41 
b.  Procedure 42 
• Load uplink test waveform (A1-1) on the RF Signal Source  43 
• Configure Signal Source to play test waveforms on 10ms frame boundaries starting when it 44 
receives a trigger signal from the CUSM-E that C-Plane messages have been sent. 45 
• Load C-Plane message sequence on Test Equipment O-RU (TER)  46 
• Arm Test Equipment O-RU (TER) to capture DUT fronthaul messages  47 
• Launch test to simultaneously play RF uplink frame and C-Plane messages  48 
• Record U-Plane messages from DUT for a complete frame and the eAxC corresponding to the 49 
Antenna port  50 
• Extract IQ information  51 
• Extract Payload 52 
• Compare payload binary sequences  53 
 54 
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  55 
1. The verdict is “Test pass” if payload binary sequences match between the uplink test frame sent to the DUT 56 
and the received U-Plane data from the DUT 57 
2. If any of the test conditions is not true, the verdict for the whole test is "Fail" 58 
3. If the DUT does not support initial conditions, the test verdict is "Inconclusive" 59

3.2.3.7.4 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Extended using reMask parameter 3GPP DL – Resource 3 
allocation 4 
A. Test Description and Applicability 5 
This test is MANDATORY. 6 
 7 
The purpose of this test is to ensure the radio can accurately interpret C-Plane resource allocation messages with 8 
the reMask parameter set, transfer U-Plane data into the correct resource elements and transmit this data 9 
accurately in the downlink.  This test is applicable for Type A and Type B radios (No precoding is required).  10 
The test will be conducted therefore there will be no channel distortion or interference.  It is mandatory the 11 
radio pass this test to be considered O-RAN conformant. 12 
 13 
This test requires non-zero data to populate all allocated resource blocks.  This data will be a PN9 sequence 14 
with a seed value of all ones.  This test is applicable for both Type A and Type B radios.  15 
 16 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 17 
 18 
• The O-RU must support the default parameters in section 3.2.1 of this document.  The test bandwidth is 20 19 
MHz Bandwidth as described by E-TM1.1. 20 
• The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port to be connected to a signal analyzer.   21 
• The signal analyzer must have the ability to decode the downlink shared channel.  22 
 23 
C. Test Methodology 24 
 25 
a. Initial Conditions 26 
• Configure the O-RU which includes collecting O-RU capabilities, configuring the O-RU for operation 27 
using M-Plane commands, and synchronizing the O-RU using G.8275.1.   28 
• Connect the signal analyzer to the O-RU antenna ports or TAB connectors under test and configure 29 
the analyzer with any set-up information needed to allow it to synch and demodulate the transmitted 30 
signal.  31 
• Let the DUT and TER to warm to the normal operating temperature within specified range.  32 
 33 
b. Procedure 34 
• Build an appropriate IQ signal describing the E-TM1.1 signal described above in the CUSM-E.   35 
• Use the CUSM-E control interface to build the appropriate C-Plane messages that describe the signal.  36 
• Every symbol should be described by a single type 1 section (DL-SCH and DCI) except symbols#6 37 
which will be used for the reMask test. 38 
• The data in this section must be a PN9 sequence using an initial seed of all ones. The first bits of the 39 
PN9 will be in PRB1 and continue in consecutive resource elements to the end of PRB5. No section 40 
type zero messages will be used for this test. 41 
• Symbol number #6 should be stock data section type “D” as shown above.   42 
• This test will only be using PRBs 1 through 5.  The corresponding C-Plane message will contain a 43 
section IDs in a single C-Plane message describing symbol #6.  44 
• The startSymbolid in the application header will be symbol #6.  45 
• The C-Plane message will have one section with the reMask set to only the odd number resource 46 
elements.  The number of PRBs will be 4. The start PRB will be 1. 47 
• The corresponding U-Plane message will be a new PN9 Sequence (initial seed is all ones) in PRBs 1 48 
through 5 of symbol #6. 49 
 50 
D. Test Requirement (expected result)  51 
1. The signal measured by the signal analyzer should satisfy a basic 3GPP signal performance requirement for 52 
this radio category (i.e., EVM). 53 
2. The test frame received by the signal analyzer should only contain the same PN9 signals that were sent in 54 
the U-Plane but only every other odd resource element. 55 
 56

3.2.3.7.5 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class With Precoding (WPR) TxD 1 
A. Test Description and Applicability 2 
This test is MANDATORY. 3 
 4 
The purpose of this test is to validate the correct implementation of transmit diversity of a Category B  O-RU with 5 
two antenna ports.  TxD uses TM2 (transmission Mode 2).  For TxD, information for 2 layers are packed into a 6 
PRB for transmission from O-DU and are unpacked at the O-RU.  TxD precoding is applied based on the C Plane 7 
configuration before RF transmission.  8 
 9 
Using a standard E-TM1.1 test frame for FDD the CUSM-E (i.e., O-RAN interface of the TER described in section 10 
3.2.2) will generate C-Plane and U-Plane messages that require the O-RU to transmit on the downlink the standard 11 
E-TM1.1 signal.   12 
 13 
This test is applicable for Type B radios only. 14 
 15

 17

MHz Bandwidth as described by E-TM1.1. 19 
• The O-RU must have a conducted antenna port to be connected to a signal analyzer.   20 
• The signal analyzer must have the ability to decode the downlink shared channel.  21 
• The O-RU must support the Section Extension ExtType=3 parameter as notified by the M -Plane 22

3.2.3.7.6 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class With Precoding (WPR) SM 8

E-TM1.1 signal.   19

3.2.3.8 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class Section Type 3 (ST3) 20 
This section will specify the test scenarios to validate the correct decoding o f C-Plane messages with section type 3. 21 
The required test setup is shown in 2.1, where only a stimulus RF signal is applied. 22 
3.2.3.8.1 UC-Plane O-RU Scenario Class ST3 Test #1: NR PRACH 23 
A. Test Description and Applicability {MANDATORY} 24 
This test is MANDATORY. 25 
This test will validate the correct decoding of C-Plane messages containing section type 3 in 5G NR scenario by 26 
testing the correct detection of a PRACH signal.  27 
TER will setup the signal generator with a PRACH test waveform according to TS 38.141 -1 section 8.4.1 and A.6. 28 
The test waveform will contain the same preamble ID repeated by following the timing offset scheme specified in 29 
the figures 8.4.1.4.2-2 or 8.4.1.4.2-3 TS 38.141-1 depending on the selected PRACH format. 30 
This is an example for FR1 – SCS=30 KHz – BW=100MHz – Format A3, at each occasion the time offset of the 31 
same preamble index (selected according to table A.6-1 TS 38.141.1) is incremented by 100nsec starting from 0 up 32 
to 800nsec (9 occasions per frame). Each PRACH occasion is at the beginning of the first nine used sub -frames. 33 
The scheme is repeated every frame. 34 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
114 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
 1 
 2 
Figure 3.2.3.8-1 FR1 SCS 30Kz 100MHz Format A3 3 
 4 
According to the PRACH waveform setting, the TER will generate a corresponding sequence of C-Plane messages 5 
with section type 3. By the corresponding U-Plane messages in the uplink direction, the TER will try to detect the 6 
presence of the corresponding preamble at the expected timing offset and calculate the probability of detection Pd 7 
according to the definition in TS38.141-1 section 8.4.1.1.  8 
The signal will be exercised at only one O-RU port without adding any external AWGN power level or multipath 9 
fading profile and at a power level avoiding detection errors due to poor SNR (rule described in the sub -section C 10 
of this scenario class). 11 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 12 
O-RU must have a conducted antenna port (FR1) or TAB connector. 13 
By the M-plane, TER will detect all the supported SCSs, FFT sizes and carrier bandwidths by the O -RU. To test 14 
the correct interpretation of section type 3, it is assumed that only one combination of the three above parameters 15 
supported by the O-RU is enough to validate the test. TER shall generate C-Plane messages according to one of the 16 
PRACH formats in table A.6-1 TS 38.141. TER will choose the format either according to the manufacturer 17 
declaration item D.103 “PRACH format and SCS” in TS 38.141-1 or according to the format information obtained 18 
by the M-plane in case O-RU implements this feature. If more formats are claimed, only one shall be selected to 19 
reduce the test time, preference will be given to a format specified in Table A.6.1 TS 38.141. It is assumed that the 20 
O-RU manufacturer will support at least one in that table. For the case of long preambles, it is assumed format 0 is 21 
always supported since the only one shown in the table A.6-1 TS 38.141.  22 
C. Test Methodology 23 
a. Initial Conditions 24 
The O-RU is synchronized using G.8275.1. The signal generator is connected to the antenna port under test and 25 
synchronized to the same frequency reference of the O-RU. CUSM-E has completed the activation of one carrier on 26 
the O-RU port and enabled one endpoint supporting section type 3. The endpoint is configured with no data 27 
compression.  28 
b. Procedure 29 
1. Set signal generator power by the following method: 30 
a. Select SNR from the scenario with two RX antennas and AWGN propagation condition in table 8.4.1.5 -31 
1, 8.4.1.5-2 or 8.4.1.5-3 TS 38.141 depending on the selected SCS and PRACH format. 32 
b. Select the AWGN power level according to the configured SCS and channel bandwidth in table 33 
8.4.1.4.2-1 TS 38.141 and multiply by the PRACH signal bandwidth.  34 


 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
115 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
c. The output power will be given by the formula (SNR+Noise power – 3dB) rounded to the first decimal 1 
digit. Extra 3dB are to compensate that SNR and noise power are selected from the two RX ports test 2 
case and this test procedure requires only one O-RU port. 3 
 4 
For example, for the FR1 – SCS=30 KHz – BW=100MHz – Format A3 SNR is -13.5dB and noise level 5 
is -70.1dBm/98.28MHz. signal generator power = -13.5dB -70.1dBm/98.28MHz*(139*30 KHz)-3dB 6 
=-19.5dBm.  7 
2. Set signal generator frequency offset to the central carrier frequency. PRACH will be mapped over frequency 8 
according to msg1-FrequencyStart ( ) parameter equal to 0. PRACH format is set according to what TER 9 
has selected from the manufacturer declarations. 10 
3. Start PRACH waveform generation on the signal generator. 11 
4. Configure CUSM-E to generate C-Plane section type 3 messages according to the PRACH occasions 12 
described in subsection A and by the following approach: 13 
a. In case of a PRACH format not including preamble repetitions, only one C-Plane message with one 14 
section ID is generated per PRACH occasion. O-DU emulator will set “cpLength” field according to 15 
table 6.3.3.1-2 or table 6.3.3.1-1 TS 38.211 and to the format specified in section 5.4.4.14 in [2] 16 
“timeOffset” field will be set according to the PRACH occasion position inside the slot and by 17 
following the format value specified section 5.4.4.12 CUS plane specification.  18 
b. In case of a PRACH format with preamble repetitions, the implementation can be achieved by one C-19 
Plane message with one section ID or by N number of C-Plane messages with one section ID 20 
corresponding to the single PRACH repetition as described in section 5.3.2 CUS plane specification. 21 
TER shall exercise both approaches and perform them in two separate test sessions by repeating steps 4 22 
and 5. 23 
c. In both scenarios “filterIndex” field is setup based on the PRACH format an d according to table 5.9 24 
of [2]and “beamId” field will set to 0 (no beamforming). 25 
5. TER will perform PRACH detection per each PRACH occasion and compare the result with the expected 26 
preamble ID and the expected timing offset. Since the external AWGN and fading generator are not present the 27 
time error tolerance should be low, TER will use the time error tolerance in table 8.4.1.1 -1 for AWGN case 28 
according to the corresponding PRACH format and PRACH SCS. A counter of successful detections is 29 
incremented at every matching. The probability of detection is given by the ratio between that counter and the 30 
number of the expected received PRACH occasions within the test time. 31 
6. Repeat the test procedure by setting msg1-FrequencyStart ( ) parameter to the right edge of the 32 
configured carrier bandwidth in order to exercise a different frequency offset number in section type 3.  33 
D. Pass/Fail Criteria (expected result) 34 
1. Test is pass if the probability of detection is 100%. 35

3.3 S-Plane Conformance Tests 2 
This Section describes tests that are used to validate S-Plane functional and performance conformance for network 3 
elements using the O-RAN WG4 fronthaul interface defined in [2] and the O-RAN WG4 mplane interface defined in 4 
[3].  This version of the conformance specification focuses on O-RU conformance tests.  Future versions of this 5 
specification will describe additional S-Plane conformance functional and performance tests for other clocks used in the 6 
front haul, e.g. O-DU, PRTC/T-GM, etc.  7 
S-Plane functionality will be determined mostly based on status retrieved from the O-RU using the M-Plane or NMS as 8 
appropriate, whereas, S-Plane performance is determined by over-the-air (OTA) or conductive (i.e. a cabled electrical 9 
connection to the DUT’s radio interface) measurements of O-RU synchronization signal. Both functional and 10 
performance tests require the provision of a test equipment i.e. provision of a test setup that includes a CUSM -plane 11 
emulator that delivers the necessary stimuli as described in section 3.3.1.1. 12 
The S-Plane conformance test suite assumes that the vendor’s equipment is conformant and has been tested to meet the 13 
requirements of G.8275.1 and IEEE1588v2 and other relevant S-Plane standards. Therefore, this document does not 14 
attempt to duplicate tests for these standards.    15 
This section provides a common high-level test scope in order to validate conformance to the synchronization plane 16 
specifications referenced by [2] section 9. Both functional and performance aspects are addressed: 17 
• The tests apply to both 4G (LTE) and 5G (NR) and are applicable to all O -RAN IOT profiles listed in Annex A 18 
• SyncE test case is optional and only valid when the SyncE slave (e.g. O-RU) takes advantage of it. Therefore, 19 
the related SyncE test cases are optional 20 
• Test cases require configuration of the DUT (e.g. O-RU). Configuration is performed using O-RAN CUSM-21 
Plane Emulator.  22 
The following bulleted notes apply specifically to functional tests in addition to the general notes above,  23 
• Shall be done in the lab at constant temperature  24 
• An CUSM-Plane emulator is needed to generate the necessary M-plane and UC-Plane background traffic in 25 
addition to S-Plane traffic that includes PTP and possibly SyncE SSM over ESMC. It is synchronized by an 26 
external test equipment or a timing master. 27 
• For validation of S-Plane, the following are used: 28 
o A CUSM-Plane emulator to send and receive synchronization information over the fronthaul interface.  29 
o A Measurement Equipment to perform frequency/phase measurements from any available synchronization 30 
interface.  31 
o DUT reports over M-Plane or NMS its S-Plane state. 32 
• The acceptance criterion for these tests is to comply with specification [2]. 33 
The following bulleted notes apply specifically to performance tests in addition to the general notes above.  34 
• To thermally stress the DUT all test shall be done in a lab at both constant and variable conditions of traffic 35 
load and temperature:  36 
o The variable thermal profile is to be defined based on the specific deployment scenario, for example, 37 
equipment deployed in a temperature-controlled location versus deployment subject to specifically 38 
characterized variable conditions. The methodology to be used to perform this test, together with an 39 
illustrative example, is described in Appendix I in ITU-T G.8273 [9] 40 
o The variable C/U-Plane profile (for example similar to test case 13 shown in figure VI.11 of ITU-T 41 
G.8261 [10]) This will be defined as part of the work on the future performance tests.  42 
o All performance tests described in this section assume the following two components in the procedure 43 
(test methodology sections): 44 
o Establishing the necessary M-plane session to bring up the O-RU and make it ready for transmission 45 
of a test signal over the air 46 
o In addition to the M-plane session, the transmission of a test signal necessitates the provision of a CU 47 
plane test vector. The test vector needs to have sufficient information to set up a sync hronization 48 
channel within the radio frame transmitted over the air. 49 
• All test cases are considered mandatory unless the test case applies to optional capabilities and the O -RU under 50 
test does not implement the applicable optional capability. 51

• The acceptance criterion for the performance tests is to satisfy the 3GPP OTA TAE limits specified in 3GPP 1 
TS 36.141 [18] for 4G (LTE) and 38.141-2 [20] for 5G (NR), and summarized in eCPRI [11] and ITU-T 2 
G.8271 [7]. The conditions applicable to each test will be set out in the relevant sections  below (future work 3 
item). 4 
• The CUS specification v3.00 [2] which follows eCPRI and IEEE802.1 CM recommendation, defines two 5 
examples of O-RU types, but these are not strict classes like the T-BC classes specified in ITU-T G.8273.2. 6

in order to execute the S-Plane conformance tests. 9
