3.3.1.1 Test Equipment Capabilities 13 
The following describes the necessary functions and capabilities of the test equipment in order to perform the tests 14 
defined in the following sections.  15 
CUSM-Plane Emulator: This function implements various planes (C, U, S, M) over transport network connecting to 16 
DUT (i.e. O-RU, O-DU). It should enable i.e. testing S-Plane performance under U-Plane stress and various noise 17 
profiles. S-Plane signals sent to DUT and measurement equipment are traceable to reference signals received from the 18 
timing master. Emulator should generate noise free reference signal for Measurement Equipment and (if required) a 19 
defined noise profile for the DUT. The CUSM-Plane emulator may be composed of multiple components or could be a 20 
single component containing all the capabilities listed below. 21 
• Reference Clock: This equipment is the frequency and time reference. It includes a PTP master and, when 22 
applicable, a SyncE master function. It delivers frequency (e.g. SyncE, 10MHz, 1PPS), phase (e.g.1PPS, 23 
10ms frame boundary) and time (e.g. Todd, PTP) signals. PRTC specified by ITU-T G.8272 is one 24 
example in terms of performance. The level of performance for these reference signals should be 25 
significantly (by an order of magnitude) better than the 3GPP synchronization requirements, when abso lute 26 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
120 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
limits are measured against the reference clock. The timing master function with the CUSM -Plane emulator 1 
is connected to a UTC traceable reference. The phase output is used to synchronize the Signal Analyzer or 2 
Test Equipment performing time error measurements. 3 
• NMS: Responsible for configuring CUSM Plane emulator to send configuration to DUT for the defined 4 
conformance tests. 5 
• M-Plane: Translate the NMS configuration into the proper M-Plane messages to correctly configure and 6 
report status from the DUT. 7 
• UC-Plane: S-Plane tests require the transmission of UC-Plane traffic over the fronthaul, the emulator shall 8 
implement the O-RAN UC-Plane protocol and shall send a stock data frame defined in Section 3.2.1.1.5 9 
and shown in Figure 3.2.1.1-1 as UC-Plane messages to DUT O-RU. 10 
• S-Plane: The CUSM-Plane emulator shall implement O-RAN S-Plane protocol.  This function should be 11 
capable of controlling the amount of noise for the PTP packets. This function should be able to degrade the 12 
clock class and add impairments on the timing signals for example insert PDV on PTP or jitter/wander on 13 
SyncE.  14 
The emulator shall merge all traffic types for transmission over the fronthaul without degrading performance of S-15 
Plane. 16 
Measurement Equipment: This equipment is responsible for extracting the desired synchronization information from 17 
the test signal transmitted by the DUT, and then measuring this information to determine if the performance is within 18 
limits. This could be a single piece of test equipment containing all the capabilities listed below, or it may be created by 19 
interconnecting a separate signal analyzer and performance measurement system.  20 
• Signal Extractor/Analyzer: This equipment demodulates the timing signal from the O-RU’s downlink 21 
radio interface. It receives RF signals from the DUT’s air or preferably coaxial interface. This equipment 22 
should be connected to Reference Clock to be able to lock on the correct synchronization channel of the O-23 
RU RF output signal. 24 
• Performance Measurement Equipment: This equipment performs time alignment error and frequency 25 
error measurements on 1pps and 10MHz signals.  It uses standard metrics to validate if measured signal 26 
meets the defined limits. It is recommended to use a ≥2 GHz sampling on 1pps signals (for 1 ns sampling 27 
accuracy)  28 
3.3.2 Functional test of O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 profile (LLS-C1/C2/C3) 29 
A. Test Description and Applicability 30 
This test is MANDATORY. 31 
The purpose of this test is to validate that an O-RU is correctly synchronizing to a CUSM Emulator delivering both 32 
PTP and (optionally) SyncE using ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] profile  and that the O -RU correctly reports its status to the 33 
CUSM Emulator based on the nominal or degraded synchronization conditions generated by CUSM Emulator.  34 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 35 
O-RU is connected to CUSM Emulator directly. The measurement equipment is connected to the O-RU’s radio 36 
interface via conducted (via an electrical connection to antenna interface) or non-conducted (via over the air radio 37 
transmission) means.  38 
O-RU must be operating with the respective NMS or M-Plane properly. (as defined in 3.2.1.1.5). 39 
C. Test Methodology 40 
a. Initial Conditions 41 
This test uses the O-RU (DUT), a CUSM-Plane emulator with NMS features to generate stimulus for the O-42 
RU (DUT) and signal analyzer to measure the radio interface timing. 43 
b. Procedure 44 
Three conditions must be tested: 45 
 46 
Startup: CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with PTP and SyncE ports in passive state (no 47 
messages sent) 48 
Nominal: CUSM-E is configured to start acting as a PTP master compliant with the ITU-T G.8275.1 [5] 49 
profile advertising LOCKED status with nominal clockClass and clockAccuracy. If SyncE is to be tested 50 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
121 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with SyncE ports in master state, compliant to ITU -T 1 
G.8264 profile advertising nominal SSM value as specified by ITU-T G.8275.1 [5]. 2 
Degraded: There are two levels of degraded conditions for both PTP and SyncE that can be configured to the 3 
CUSM-Emulator. 4 
• The first degradation level is where the CUSM-E is configured to act as a clock, with PTP and SyncE 5 
ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T G.8275.1 profile, and sending configured clockClass and/or 6 
SSM values within the O-RU’s configured accepted limits via the M-plane.  7 
• The second degradation level is where the same clockClass and/or SSM values are sent by CUSM -E 8 
outside the O-RU’s configured accepted limits via the M-plane. 9 
To cover the all the relevant scenarios the test sequence listed in Table 3.3.2-3.3.1.1-1 steps through the 10 
Startup/Nominal/Degraded states in a sequence.  The steps in this table and Table 3.3.2-3.3.1.1-2 are intended 11 
to be exercised in sequential order.  Since SyncE is optional, there are two columns, one for PTP status and a 12 
second for SyncE.  Each of the status items corresponds the conditions  defined above. 13

The acceptance criterion is that the status reported by the O-RU for the steps defined in above procedure matches 18 
the results described in Table 3.3.2-3.3.1.1-2.   The left column indicates the steps defined in Table 3.3.2-3.3.1.1-1. 19

plane clock status parameters that are queried from the test O-RU and their desired value. For PTP clockClass and 21 
optional SyncE SSM quality level, the “Received Value” is the one received by the O -RU (except in Startup mode 22 
when there is no such received value and the default one is reported). 23 
The O-RU Sync-state, PTP lock state, PTP state, PTP clock-class, SyncE lock-state, SyncE state, SyncE quality-24 
level are defined in the M-Plane specification [3] (chapter 10) and relevant YANG models.  25

3.3.3 Performance test of O-RU using ITU-T G.8275.1 Profile (LLS-C1/C2/C3) 7 
A. Test Description and Applicability 8 
This test is MANDATORY.   9 
This test validates that an O-RU is synchronizing from a CUSM-plane Emulator delivering configured (ideal and 10 
normal operating conditions) PTP and (optionally) SyncE. Frequency and time error generated by the O-RU must 11 
be within specified limits.  12 
This test focuses on LLS-C1.  In this edition of the document this test can provisionally apply to LLS -C2, but some 13 
details related to frequency error require further study.  LLS-C3 will be addressed in a future version. 14 
CUS -plane spec lists two classes of O-DU (class A has ±15 ppb frequency error limit; class B has ±5 ppb limit). 15 
This test applies to the strictest one from O-RU prospective and therefore considers class A O-DU. 16 
B. Test Entrance Criteria 17 
O-RU is connected to CUSM-Plane Emulator via direct fiber link(s).  18 
Conformance Functional test 2.5.2 is successfully passed. 19 
It is the vendor’s responsibility to make sure that limits defined in the test are also met in worse -case field 20 
conditions.  Thermal testing, PTP PDV tolerance and SyncE jitter/wander tolerance are beyond the scope of this 21 
test. 22 
O-RU must be operating with the respective NMS or M-Plane properly. (as defined in 3.2.1.1.5). 23 
C. Test Methodology 24 
a. Initial Conditions 25 
These tests use the O-RU DUT and a CUSM-Plane emulator with NMS features.   26 

 
________________________________________________________________________________________________ 
Copyright © 2020 by the O-RAN Alliance. 
Your use is subject to the terms of the O-RAN Adopter License Agreement in Annex ZZZ           
124 
                                                                                          O-RAN.WG4.CONF.0-v01.00 
Frequency and time error are measured on the Air interface at the O-RU output. 1 
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with PTP ports in master state, compliant to ITU-T 2 
G.8275.1 profile advertising LOCKED status with nominal clockClass and clockAccuracy.  3 
CUSM-Plane Emulator is configured to act as a clock, with SyncE ports in master state, compliant to ITU -4 
T G.8264 profile advertising nominal SSM value.  5 
The DUT shall have achieved frequency and phase lock prior to starting the test.  6 
b. Procedure:  7 
Unlike the functional test defined in section 3.3.2, where start-up / nominal / degraded scenarios are tested, 8 
only nominal scenarios with ideal and normal operation input noise are tested in this section.  9 
1. Ideal: PTP and SyncE (if used) provide “ideal” O-RU input synchronization with no added noise. 10 
2. Normal Operation: PTP and SyncE (if used) provide “Within normal operating limits” O -RU inputs 11 
as specified in CUS-Plane Specification [1], simultaneously meeting two limits:  12 
a. PTP and SyncE maximum time error: ± 1400 ns,  13 
b. PTP and SyncE maximum frequency error (0.1Hz low pass filtered): ±15 ppb  14 
Notes applicable to this Normal Operation condition test: 15 
- The CUSM-Plane Emulator may be configured to generate the time and frequency error of PTP and 16 
SyncE, either simultaneously or sequence.  17 
- CU and M plane messages do not need to be modified. It has no impact if they are delayed by the 18 
time and frequency error applied in this test. 19 
- The time error added to the input signal shall follow a sinusoidal waveform with amplitude (A) and 20 
frequency (f). Three such signal frequencies are specified for the test, but intermediate ones can be 21 
used for testing, as long as the following relationship between amplitude and frequency: A[ns] = 22 
15[ppb]/(2*pi*f[Hz]) is maintained and simultaneously meet the 2a and 2b conditions above. An 23 
additional constant time error may be added to the sinusoidal waveform for each frequency, so th at 24 
the maximum time error reaches the maximum value of + 1400 ns: cTE [ns] = 1400[ns]  - A[ns]. 25 
- The conditions listed in Table 3.3.3-3.3.1.1-1 are 20 ns lower than the total limit of 1420 ns to 26 
accommodate measurement errors, noise transfer not specified.  27 
- Based on ITU-T analysis it is considered that the time error budget comprises both constant and 28 
dynamic errors. Because of this the time error budget is proposed to be split so that the constant time 29 
error represents at least half of the total budget. This is approximately consistent with ITU -T 8271.1. 30 
- Testing any higher frequency input noise than the ITU cut-off frequency (0.1Hz) would require using 31 
limits that are defined by vendor-specific parameters (CUS spec provides an example for a 75mhz 32 
low pass filtering and 18ppb frequency noise generation O-RU). It is therefore outside the scope of 33 
this document and such performance must be validated by vendors and documented in test reports. 34 
- The following table and graph show the three sinusoidal time error waveforms to be used for testing:  35 
 36 
 37 
Frequency [Hz] Dynamic Time Error  
Amplitude [ns] 
Constant Time

D. Pass/Fail Criteria (expected results)  4 
The results as measured for conducted or non-conducted (OTA) on the Air interface from the two conditions 5 
specified above shall be less than or equal to these values:  6 
1. Ideal Case:  7 
a. ±35 ppb maximum frequency error  8 
(3GPP limit 50 ppb - 15ppb = 35 ppb, where 15ppb is the error of a class A O-DU (worst-case)) 9 
b. +/-80ns maximum time error 10 
(3GPP limit 1500 ns – CUS spec 1420ns = 80 ns, where 1420ns is the error allocated to the O-DU for 11 
LLS-C1).   12 
c. As multiple O-RUs are not tested, there is no distinction between relative and absolute time error 13 
measurement. 14 
2. Normal Operation Case:  15 
a. ±50 ppb maximum frequency error  16 
(3GPP limit) 17 
b. ±1500ns maximum time error 18 
(3GPP limit).  19 
As multiple O-RUs are not tested, there is no distinction between relative and absolute time error measurement.  20

4.1 This Agreement shall remain in force, unless early terminated according to this Section 4.  21 
4.2 O-RAN Alliance on behalf of its Members, Contributors and Academic Contributors may terminate this Agreement 22 
if Adopter materially breaches this Agreement and does not cure or is not capable of curing such breach within thirty 23

4.3 Sections 1, 3, 5 - 11 of this Agreement shall survive any termination of this Agreement. Under surviving Section 3, 25 
after termination of this Agreement, Adopter will continue to grant licenses (a) to entities who become Adopters after 26 
the date of termination; and (b) for future versions of ORAN Specifications that are backwards compatible with the 27 
version that was current as of the date of termination. 28 
Section 5: CONFIDENTIALITY 29 
Adopter will use the same care and discretion to avoid disclosure, publication, and dissemination of O -RAN 30 
Specifications to third parties, as Adopter employs with its own confidential information, but no less than reasonable 31 
care. Any disclosure by Adopter to its Affiliates, contractors and consultants should be subject to an obligation of 32 
confidentiality at least as restrictive as those contained in this Section. The foregoing obligation shall not apply to any 33 
information which is: (1) rightfully known by Adopter without any limitation on use or disclosure prior to disclosure; 34 
(2) publicly available through no fault of Adopter; (3) rightfully received without a duty of confidentiality; (4) disclosed 35 
by O-RAN Alliance or a Member, Contributor or Academic Contributor to a third party without a duty of 36 
confidentiality on such third party; (5) independently developed b y Adopter; (6) disclosed pursuant to the order of a 37 
court or other authorized governmental body, or as required by law, provided that Adopter provides reasonable prior 38 
written notice to O-RAN Alliance, and cooperates with O-RAN Alliance and/or the applicable Member, Contributor or 39 
Academic Contributor to have the opportunity to oppose any such order; or (7) disclosed by Adopter with O -RAN 40 
Alliance’s prior written approval. 41
